Second Proof: Allah's Action Has No Cause
Imam Razi presents the second proof using a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof that Allah's action cannot have a cause, using the dilemma of an eternal or originated cause, and the principle of the scholars of usul.

Core Idea
Allah's making has no cause; it is the cause of everything else.

Imam Razi presents a clear dilemma: if Allah's action (His causing-to-exist) had a cause, that cause must either be eternal or originated. Both options lead to impossibility. This proof reinforces the fundamental theological principle that Allah's will and action are uncaused, as stated by the masters of usul.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the structure: a premise followed by two branches.
The passage uses a classical dilemma format.
2
Follow the dilemma
Identify the two possibilities: an eternal cause and an originated cause. For each, notice the consequence that makes it impossible.
Eternal cause leads to eternal action (contradiction). Originated cause leads to infinite regress.
3
Connect to the usul principle
The passage ends by quoting the masters of usul. Compare this principle with the conclusion of the dilemma: Allah's making has no cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية: لو كانت موجدية الله تعالى معللة بعلة لكانت تلك العلة. إن كانت قديمة لزم من قدمها قدم الفعل وهو محال. وإن كانت محدثة، افتقر كونه تعالى موجدا لتلك العلة إلى علة أخرى فيلزم التسلسل وهو محال. وهذا هو المراد من قول مشايخ الأصول (علة كل شيء صنعه ولا علة لصنعه).
The second proof: If the causing-to-exist (mujidiyyah) of God Almighty were based on a cause, then that cause: if it were eternal (qadim), then from its eternity would follow the eternity of the action, which is impossible. And if it were originated (muhdath), then His being a cause for that cause would depend on another cause, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul), which is impossible. This is the meaning of the statement of the masters of usul: 'The cause of everything is His making, and there is no cause for His making.'
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This is the second proof against divine actions having causes. It is a dilemma: if Allah's causing-to-exist had a cause, that cause must be either eternal or originated. If eternal, the action caused would also be eternal, but the world is originated, so impossible. If originated, then Allah's act of being a cause for that cause would need another cause, leading to an infinite chain, also impossible. Thus, Allah's action has no cause. The author cites the principle of the scholars of usul: 'The cause of everything is His making, and there is no cause for His making.'

Key Terms
موجدية
علة
قديم
محدث
تسلسل
صنعه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof implies that Allah acts arbitrarily without wisdom or purpose.
Correction: The proof only denies that Allah's action has an external cause that necessitates it; it does not deny that Allah acts with wisdom and for a purpose, as per Islamic teachings.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, if the cause of Allah's action were originated, what would follow?
A) The action would be eternal
B) Infinite regress
C) The cause would be eternal
D) Allah would be imperfect

Key Takeaway
Allah's causing-to-exist has no cause, for any cause would lead to an impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's action has no cause, then everything in your life—your success, your trials, your very existence—is directly from Him without any intermediate necessity. How does this truth change the way you view the difficulties you are facing right now, and what will you do today to express that dependence?
?
The scholars said, 'The cause of everything is His making, and there is no cause for His making.' This means that nothing in the universe forces Allah to do anything. Your sins do not cause Him to punish you, nor do your good deeds cause His reward—they are entirely from His generosity. Knowing that you cannot obligate Allah, what should be the foundation of your hope and fear? Write down one specific fear you have about your afterlife and answer it using this teaching.
?
Consider the infinite regress argument: every cause needs a cause unless you stop at the Uncaused Cause. You are a created being, contingent. If you were to rely on created things as your ultimate causes—money, status, people—you would be chasing an infinite chain that never ends. What is one created 'cause' you have been relying on as if it were ultimate, and how will you redirect your trust to the Uncaught Cause today?

4 min
The Second Proof: No Cause for God's Creative Act
Second proof by Razi against a cause for God's creative act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's act of creation cannot have a cause, based on the argument from infinite regress and the dichotomy of eternal/temporal causes.

Core Idea
God's making is the cause of all things, but itself has no cause.

Imam Razi presents a second proof that God's creative act cannot be caused. He argues that any supposed cause would either be eternal or temporal, both leading to impossibility. This lesson walks through the logical steps of this foundational argument, which is a cornerstone of Ash'ari theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and its translation
Read the original Arabic text once without trying to analyze it. Then read the literal translation to understand the surface meaning.
Notice that Razi uses a very concise style.
2
Identify the two possibilities for the cause
The proof divides the hypothetical cause into two cases: eternal or temporal. Find these in the text and note the reasoning for each.
This is a classic logical division (taqsim).
3
Trace the consequences of each possibility
For each case, see why it leads to an impossibility: eternal cause leads to eternal act (invalid because the world is temporal), temporal cause leads to infinite regress (invalid).
Both branches lead to impossibility, proving the original assumption (that there is a cause) is false.
4
Understand the concluding principle
Razi ends by quoting the masters: 'The cause of everything is His making, and there is no cause for His making.' This summarizes the proof's conclusion.
This principle is a key Ash'ari doctrine affirming God's absolute sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : لو كانت موجدية الله تعالى معللة بعلة لكانت تلك العلة . إن كانت قديمة لزم من قدمها قدم الفعل وهو محال . وإن كانت محدثة، افتقر كونه تعالى موجدا لتلك العلة إلى علة أخرى فيلزم التسلسل وهو محال. وهذا هو المراد من قول مشايخ الأصول (علة كل شيء صنعه ولا علة لصنعه).
The second proof: If God's bringing-into-existence were motivated by a cause, then that cause: if it were eternal, then its eternality would necessitate the eternality of the act, which is impossible. And if it were temporal, then His being the bringer-into-existence of that cause would depend on another cause, leading to an infinite regress, which is impossible. This is the meaning of the saying of the masters of usul: 'The cause of everything is His making, and there is no cause for His making.'
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof, which is a classic argument against any cause for God's creative act. The proof divides the supposed cause into two possibilities: it is either eternal or temporal. If the cause is eternal, then its effect (the act of creation) would also be eternal, which is impossible because the world is temporal. If the cause is temporal, then there must be a cause that brought that cause into existence, and that cause in turn would need another cause, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul), which is impossible. Therefore, God's act of bringing things into existence cannot have a cause. The author cites the principle of the masters of usul: 'The cause of everything is His making, and there is no cause for His making.' This means God's act of creation is the ultimate cause of all other things, but itself has no cause.

Key Terms
موجدية
علة
قديمة
محدثة
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof denies that God acts with wisdom or purpose.
Correction: The proof only denies that there is a separate cause that compels God to act; it does not deny wisdom or purpose in His actions.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, what does the saying 'علة كل شيء صنعه ولا علة لصنعه' mean?
A) Everything has a cause except God.
B) God's act of making is the cause of everything, and that making itself has no cause.
C) The universe has no cause.
D) God's actions are random.

Key Takeaway
God's act of creation is the ultimate cause of everything, but itself has no cause, as shown by the impossibility of an eternal cause or an infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself demanding a reason from God for His actions in your life, as if He owes you an explanation? How does this proof challenge that attitude?
?
If God's act of creation has no cause beyond His own will, then everything that happens is directly from Him. Are you ready to accept that even the hardships you face are without external cause, but purely from His wisdom? Would that change how you respond to them?
?
This proof shows that infinite regress is impossible. In your own spiritual life, are there excuses or justifications you keep leaning on that lead to an endless cycle? What would it mean to stop that regress and submit fully to God's act?

The Fourth Proof: Temporal Specification Leads to Regress
Razi argues that specifying a time for creation involves an impossible regress

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses a temporal specification argument to prove that God's creation is not motivated by external purposes.

Core Idea
If creation had a purpose, it would lead to infinite regress—so God's will is self-sufficient.

Imam al-Razi presents his fourth proof against the claim that God's actions are motivated by purposes. He examines the specific timing of creation and shows that any attempt to assign a purpose leads to logical contradictions. This argument is a classic example of reductio ad absurdum in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully to grasp the overall argument. Note the two main possibilities Razi considers.
The argument is dense; reading it twice may help.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Razi splits the case into two: either the purpose existed before the world or it occurred at the same time. Identify these in the text.
3
Trace the consequences of each
For the first possibility, see why it leads to absurdity. For the second, note the sub-case about whether the purpose needs an originator.
Pay attention to the logical steps.
4
Follow the regress argument
If the purpose needs an originator, that originator's act would also need a purpose, leading to infinite regress. Understand why this is impossible.
This is the key move in the proof.
5
Reach the conclusion
If no further purpose is needed, then God's creative act is independent of purposes. Razi notes this applies to all events.
This is the desired conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : أنه لو وجب أن يكون خلقه وحكمه معللا بغرض، لكان خلق الله تعالى العلم في وقت معين دون ما قبله وما بعده معللا برعاية مصلحة وغرض . ذلك الغرض - وتلك المصلحة - إما أن يقال إنه كان حاصلا قبل ذلك الوقت ، وإما كان حاصلا قبله. فإن كان حاصلا قبله كان ما لأجله أوجد الله تعالى العالم في ذلك الوقت حاصلا قبل أن أوجده فيلزم أن يقال: إنه كان موجدا له قبل أن كان موجدا وذلك محال وأما إن قلنا بأن ذلك الغرض وتلك المصلحة ما كان حاصلا قبل ذلك الوقت، وإنما حدث في ذلك الوقت، فنقول : حصول ذلك الغرض في ذلك الوقت، إما أن يفتقر إلى المحدث أولا يفتقر. فإن لم يفتقر فقد حدث لشيء، لا عن موجد ومحدث وهو محال. وإن افتقر إلى المحدث. فإن افتقر تخصيص إحداث ذلك الغرض بذلك الوقت إلى غرض آخر، عاد التقسيم الأول فيه ولزم التسلسل وإن لم يفتقر البتة إلى رعاية غرض آخر، فحينئذ تكون موجدية الله تعالى وخالقيته غنية عن التعليل بالأغراض والمصالح . وهذا هو المطلوب. واعلم : أن هذه الحجة التي ذكرناها في اختصاص حدوث العالم بذلك الوقت المعين عائدة في اختصاص كل واحد من الحوادث لوقته المعين.
The fourth proof: If it were necessary that His creation and judgment be motivated by a purpose, then God's creation of the world at a specific time, not before or after, would be motivated by consideration of a benefit and purpose. That purpose and benefit: either it is said that it existed before that time, or it existed before it. If it existed before it, then that for the sake of which God brought the world into existence at that time existed before He brought it into existence, so it would be necessary to say that He was bringing it into existence before He was bringing it into existence, and that is impossible. And if we say that that purpose and benefit did not exist before that time, but occurred at that time, then we say: The occurrence of that purpose at that time either needs an originator or does not need it. If it does not need it, then it occurred without an originator and creator, which is impossible. And if it needs an originator, then if specifying the occurrence of that purpose at that time needs another purpose, the first division returns in it and an infinite regress follows. And if it does not need at all consideration of another purpose, then God's being the bringer-into-existence and creator is independent of motivation by purposes and benefits. And this is what is sought. And know: that this proof which we have mentioned concerning the specification of the world's occurrence at that specific time applies to the specification of each individual event to its specific time.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof, which focuses on the temporal specification of events. The author argues that if God's creation is for a purpose, then the creation of the world at a specific time must be for a purpose that existed either before the world or at the time of creation. If the purpose existed before the world, then God would be bringing the world into existence for something that already existed, which is absurd (it would imply He was already doing it). If the purpose came into existence at the same time as the world, then that purpose itself must have a cause. If it has no cause, it appears spontaneously, which is impossible. If it has a cause, that cause's specification to that time again requires a purpose, leading to an infinite regress. If, on the other hand, the purpose does not require another purpose for its specification, then God's creative act is independent of purposes, which is the desired conclusion. The author notes that this argument applies not only to the creation of the world but to every individual event at its specific time.

Key Terms
غرض
مصلحة
تخصيص
تسلسل
محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof denies that God acts at specific times.
Correction: The proof actually denies that those times are chosen for external reasons; God's will itself is sufficient.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the fourth proof?
A) God cannot create at a specific time.
B) God's creative act is independent of purposes.
C) The world must be eternal.
D) Every event has a purpose.

Key Takeaway
Razi's fourth proof uses a dilemma to show that if creation were for a purpose, it would lead to absurdity or infinite regress, thus God's creative act is not motivated by external purposes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult situation, do you instinctively look for a 'purpose' behind it—something God must be trying to teach you? What would it mean to trust that His will alone is sufficient, even without understanding any benefit? Can you actually live that way starting today?
?
The proof argues that God's actions are not motivated by purposes you could grasp. Does that unsettle you? Examine your need to see reasons for everything God does. Are you willing to submit to His will without demanding an explanation? What would that look like in your next trial?
?
Suppose you never learn why a particular hardship happened. Would you still believe God is wise and good? Or does your faith depend on having answers? Confront that question honestly—not theoretically, but in your heart. What needs to change so that God's self-sufficient will is enough for you?

Allah's Actions Are Beyond Causes and Purposes
Imam al-Razi presents a concise argument denying causes and purposes for Allah's actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Muslim theologians deny that Allah's actions are motivated by external causes or purposes.

Core Idea
Allah's actions are too perfect to be explained by causes or purposes.

This passage from Imam al-Razi presents a concise argument establishing that Allah's actions are not driven by external purposes. The reasoning is simple but profound: if using a means to achieve a goal is considered futile, then such futility cannot be attributed to Allah. Therefore, Allah's actions are beyond being explained by causes or purposes. Let's read the original text and unpack its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage is very short but dense.
2
Identify key terms
Look for the Arabic terms: توسل (resorting to a means), عبث (futility), علل (causes), أغراض (purposes). These are central to the argument.
These terms appear in the conclusion.
3
Follow the logical flow
The passage has two parts: a conditional premise and a conclusion. Trace how the premise leads to the conclusion.
The argument is based on the impossibility of futility for Allah.
4
Reflect on the broader significance
Consider why this argument matters for Islamic theology. It defends Allah's transcendence and independence from external influences.
This does not deny wisdom in Allah's actions, only external motivation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابتداء : كان التوسل إلى تحصيل ذلك المطلوب بتلك الواسطة عبثا، وذلك على الله تعالى محال . فثبت أنه لا يمكن تعليل أفعاله وأحكامه بشيء من العلل والأغراض.
Beginning: If resorting to a means to obtain that goal is futile, then that is impossible for Allah Most High. So it is established that it is not possible to give a cause or purpose for His actions and judgments.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents a concise argument that Allah's actions cannot be explained by causes and purposes. The author begins by stating a general principle: if using a means to achieve a goal is futile, then such a means cannot be attributed to Allah, who is perfect and free from futility. From this, the conclusion is drawn that it is impossible to assign any causes (علل) or purposes (أغراض) to His actions and rulings. The argument is straightforward and relies on the absurdity of attributing futile means to Allah.

Key Terms
توسل
عبث
علل
أغراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's actions have no purpose or wisdom at all.
Correction: The passage only denies that Allah's actions are motivated by external causes or purposes, not that they lack wisdom. Allah's actions are wise but not driven by external factors.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of this passage?
A) Allah's actions are motivated by purposes that benefit Him
B) It is impossible to attribute causes and purposes to Allah's actions
C) Allah's actions are futile
D) Resorting to means is necessary for Allah

Key Takeaway
Allah's actions are not driven by external causes or purposes, for that would imply futility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial you cannot understand, do you find yourself searching for a 'reason' or 'purpose' behind it? How does this lesson challenge your need to know the 'why' before you submit?
?
Have you ever caught yourself thinking, 'Allah did this because I did that'? How does this lesson refine your understanding of the relationship between your actions and Allah's decree?
?
If Allah's actions are not driven by purposes, does that make Him seem distant or unrelatable to you? How can you still trust His actions while surrendering the need to see a purpose?

The Fourth Proof: Refuting Purposes in Creation
Razi's fourth proof against purposes in creation, focusing on timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that refutes the claim that Allah's creation is motivated by purposes, specifically by analyzing the timing of creation.

Core Idea
Allah's creative power is independent of purposes; purposes lead to absurdity or infinite regress.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi presents a sophisticated logical proof that challenges the idea that Allah creates for purposes. By focusing on the specific timing of creation—why now rather than earlier or later—he demonstrates that assuming a purpose leads to contradictions or an infinite chain of purposes. This proof is a cornerstone of Ash'ari theology, affirming that Allah's actions are not constrained by external interests.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the logical structure and the two main branches of the argument.
The proof is dense; take your time to follow each step.
2
Understand the first possibility
Examine the branch where the purpose existed before creation. Razi shows this leads to a contradiction: Allah would have created before He created.
This is an impossibility (muhal).
3
Understand the second possibility
Now trace the second branch: the purpose arises at the time of creation. This splits into two sub-branches: whether the purpose itself needs a creator or not. Follow each sub-branch to its conclusion.
Note that infinite regress is also impossible, so the only consistent outcome is independence from purposes.
4
Reflect on the conclusion and generalization
The proof ends with the conclusion that Allah's creative power is independent (mustaghni) of purposes. Razi then notes that the same argument applies to every event's specific time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : أنه لو وجب أن يكون خلقه وحكمه معللا بغرض، لكان خلق الله تعالى العلم في وقت معين دون ما قبله وما بعده معللا برعاية مصلحة وغرض . ذلك الغرض - وتلك المصلحة - إما أن يقال إنه كان حاصلا قبل ذلك الوقت ، وإما كان حاصلا قبله. فإن كان حاصلا ،قبله كان ما لأجله أوجد الله تعالى العالم في ذلك الوقت حاصلا قبل أن أوجده فيلزم أن يقال: إنه كان موجدا له قبل أن كان موجدا وذلك محال وأما إن قلنا بأن ذلك الغرض وتلك المصلحة ما كان حاصلا قبل ذلك الوقت، وإنما حدث في ذلك الوقت، فنقول : حصول ذلك الغرض في ذلك الوقت، إما أن يفتقر إلى المحدث أولا يفتقر. فإن لم يفتقر فقد حدث لشيء، ، لا عن موجد ومحدث وهو محال. وإن افتقر إلى المحدث. فإن افتقر تخصيص إحداث ذلك الغرض بذلك الوقت إلى غرض آخر، عاد التقسيم الأول فيه ولزم التسلسل وإن لم يفتقر البتة إلى رعاية غرض آخر، فحينئذ تكون موجدية الله تعالى وخالقيته غنية عن التعليل بالأغراض والمصالح . وهذا هو المطلوب. واعلم : أن هذه الحجة التي ذكرناها في اختصاص حدوث العالم بذلك الوقت المعين عائدة في اختصاص كل واحد من الحوادث لوقته المعين.
The fourth proof: If His creation and judgment must be motivated by a purpose, then the creation of knowledge by Allah Most High at a specific time rather than before or after would be motivated by consideration of an interest and purpose. That purpose and interest – either it is said that it existed before that time, or it existed before it. If it existed before it, then what for the sake of which Allah brought the world into existence at that time existed before He brought it into existence, so it would be necessary to say: He was bringing it into existence before He brought it into existence, which is impossible. And if we say that that purpose and interest did not exist before that time, but rather occurred at that time, we say: The occurrence of that purpose at that time either needs a creator or does not need. If it does not need, then it occurred without an originator and creator, which is impossible. And if it needs a creator, then if the specification of the creation of that purpose at that time needs another purpose, the first division returns to it and infinite regress follows; and if it in no way needs consideration of another purpose, then the power of Allah Most High to create and originate is independent of motivation by purposes and interests. And that is the desired conclusion. And know: that this proof which we have mentioned concerning the specification of the occurrence of the world at that particular time applies to the specification of every event at its particular time.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage contains the fourth proof, a detailed logical argument demonstrating that Allah's creation cannot be motivated by any purpose, specifically regarding the timing of creation. The proof proceeds by considering a supposed purpose for why Allah created the world at a particular time. Two possibilities are examined: either the purpose existed before that time or it came into existence at that time. If it existed before, then creation should have occurred earlier, leading to a contradiction. If it came into existence at that time, then either it requires a creator or not. If it does not require a creator, that is impossible. If it does require a creator, then further examination leads either to another purpose (creating infinite regress) or to the conclusion that Allah's creative power is independent of purposes. Thus, the claim of purpose is refuted. The note extends this reasoning to all events, generalizing the proof.

Key Terms
غرض
مصلحة
تسلسل
موجدية
خالقية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof denies that Allah's actions have any wisdom or benefit.
Correction: The proof only denies that Allah's actions are necessitated by external purposes; it does not deny that they have wisdom or benefit from our perspective.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the purpose for creation existed before creation?
A) Creation would occur at the right time
B) Allah would be bringing into existence before He brings into existence
C) The purpose would not need a creator
D) Infinite regress would occur

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof establishes that Allah's creative action is not motivated by external purposes, as such purposes lead to logical absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face trials, do you find yourself demanding a 'purpose' from Allah, as if He owes you an explanation? How does Razi's proof challenge that attitude, and what would it mean to surrender your need for a reason and trust His absolute independence?
?
The proof shows that purposes lead to logical absurdities. Have you ever assumed that Allah must act according to your sense of justice or fairness? How can you reshape your understanding of divine actions to accept that His wisdom may be beyond your comprehension, yet still real?
?
Razi concludes that Allah's creative power is independent of purposes. Does this make you uncomfortable? Reflect: Is your belief in Allah's wisdom based on your own ability to see purposes, or on submission to His will? What would it take to let go of the need to justify His actions?

Causality and Created Things

The Fifth Proof: Only Allah Creates, So No Purposes
A concise deductive proof from Allah's sole creative agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the doctrine that Allah alone creates leads to the conclusion that His actions are not motivated by interests or purposes.

Core Idea
Allah's exclusive creative power means His acts are free from external purposes.

In this fifth proof, Imam Razi builds on a foundational principle established earlier: only Allah is the true creator of all things. From this, he deduces that good and evil, faith and disbelief are all brought into existence by Allah. This leads to a crucial theological point: Allah's attribute as Creator cannot be contingent upon considerations of benefit or purpose, because that would imply a dependency outside of Him.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise: creation of actions
The proof begins by referencing the earlier discussion on 'خلق الأفعال' (creation of actions) which established that only Allah brings things into existence. Recognize that this is the foundational belief that all actions, whether good or evil, are created by Allah.
This premise is not argued here; it is taken as established.
2
See the implication: all moral opposites from Allah
Once you accept that only Allah creates, then everything—good and evil, disbelief and faith—occurs by His creation. Notice that this includes both what humans consider beneficial and harmful.
3
Grasp the conclusion: no purpose attached to divine creation
If all things come from Allah, then His act of creation cannot be dependent on achieving some purpose or interest (مصلحة). Otherwise, His creative power would be limited by external considerations.
The proof is concise: premise → implication → conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : قد بينا في مسألة خلق الأفعال أنه لا موجد إلا الله تعالى، وإذا كان كذلك كان الخير والشر والكفر والإيمان حاصلا بإيجاده وتخليقه وتكوينه . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك امتنع توقف كونه تعالى خالقا وموجدا على رعاية المصالح والأغراض. عنه.
The fifth proof: We have explained in the issue of the creation of actions that there is no creator except Allah Most High. If that is so, then good and evil, disbelief and faith occur by His creation, formation, and bringing into being. And if the matter is so, it is impossible that His being a creator and originator is dependent on consideration of interests and purposes. [End of proof].
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof, which is more concise. It builds on the earlier-established doctrine (in the issue of 'خلق الأفعال' or creation of actions) that Allah is the sole creator. If only Allah creates, then everything—including good, evil, disbelief, and faith—comes from Him. Consequently, His role as creator cannot be conditioned on considerations of benefit or purpose (مصالح وأغراض). The proof is straightforward: since He is the only creator, His creative act is absolute and not reliant on any external motivation.

Key Terms
خلق الأفعال
موجد
خالق
مصالح
أغراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof denies human moral responsibility for actions.
Correction: The proof focuses solely on the creative agency of Allah, not on human accountability. It does not negate human free will or moral responsibility; it only asserts that all actions are ultimately created by Allah.

Checkpoint
On what prior discussion does this proof rely?
A) The proof of prophethood
B) The issue of the creation of actions
C) The unity of Allah
D) The attributes of Allah

Key Takeaway
Allah's exclusive creative power implies that His actions are not constrained by external purposes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a painful trial, do you instinctively search for a 'purpose' behind it, as if Allah needed reason? What would it mean for your submission if you accepted that His decree is simply from His exclusive creation, not for any fathomable purpose?
?
If every good and evil in your life—including your own faith and disbelief—is directly created by Allah, does that make you feel relieved or terrified? Why?
?
Are you willing to let go of the need to understand 'why' things happen, trusting that Allah's creative power is not dependent on any purpose you can comprehend? What would that look like in your daily worries?

The Present Part of Motion is Indivisible in Time
Razi proves the present part of motion is temporally indivisible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that the present part of motion must be temporally indivisible, which is the first step in proving atomic composition.

Core Idea
Motion's existence requires a temporally indivisible present part.

Razi begins his proof by analyzing the nature of motion as an attribute that becomes present after absence. He argues that for motion to exist at all, there must be some part of it present in the current moment, and that part cannot be divided in time. This foundational step leads to the conclusion that motion is composed of discrete temporal units.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read Razi's Arabic text and its translation. Notice how he sets up a dilemma: either nothing of motion is present, or something is. He eliminates the first option.
Pay attention to the logical structure: conditional premise, proof of antecedent.
2
Identify the key dilemma
Razi asks: does motion have any part present in the current moment? If not, it cannot be past or future, so motion would be non-existent—a contradiction. So there must be a present part.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Examine the indivisibility argument
Razi then argues that this present part cannot be temporally divisible. If it were, only a half would be present at any instant, contradicting its being wholly present. Thus it is indivisible.
He uses the idea that temporal division implies parts that are not simultaneous.
4
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that the present part of motion is a temporal atom—a minimal unit that does not accept further temporal division.
This sets up the next lesson on spatial atoms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الأولى : إن كانت الحركة مركبة من أمور متتالية كل واحد منها لا يقبل القسمة الزمانية بوجه من الوجوه كان الجسم مركبا من أمور كل واحد منها لا يقبل القسمة الزمانية بوجه من الوجوه والمقدم حق فالتالي مثله. وإنما قلنا : إن الحركة مركبة من أمور متتالية كل واحد منها لا يقبل القسمة الزمانية، وذلك لأن الجسم يشاهد أنه تحرك بعد أن لم يكن متحركا. وهذه الحركة صفة زائدة على ذات الجسم. ثم نقول : هذه الصفة إما أن لا يحصل شيء منها في الحال، أو يحصل. فإن لم يحصل شيء منها في الحال امتنع أن يصير ماضيا أو مستقبلا. وذلك لأن الماضي هو الذي كان حاضرا في وقت من الأوقات. وقد زال الآن. والمستقبل هو الذي يتوقع أن يحضر في زمان من الأزمنة الآتية، وبعد لم يحضر. فلو امتنع أن يكون له حضور بوجه من الوجوه، لم يكن ماضيا، ولا مستقبلا ولا حاضرا. وكل ما كان كذلك لم يكن موجودا البتة. فالحركة لا وجود لها البتة. وهذا خلف. فثبت أنه لا بد أن يحضر من الحركة شيء في الحال. وذلك الحاضر في الحال إما أن يقبل القسمة بحسب الزمان أو لا يقبل فإن قبلها افترض فيه جزءان أحدهما قبل الآخر، لأن القسمة الزمانية هكذا تكون وحين ما كان النصف الأول موجودًا ، لم يكن النصف الثاني حاضرا، وحينما جاء النصف الثاني، صار النصف الأول فانيا، وحينئذ لا يكون الحاضر الموجود حاضرًا موجودا ، بل الحاضر الموجود منه نصفه . ثم نعيد التقسيم الأول في ذلك النصف. والحاصل أن كل ما كان منقسما بحسب القسمة الزمانية، لم يكن مجموعه موجودًا، وما كان مجموعا حاضرًا وجب أن لا يكون منقسما بحسب القسمة الزمانية فثبت أن الحاضر من الحركة والحاصل منها في الحال غير قابل للقسمة الزمانية. إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إذا انقضى ذلك الجزء حصل عقيب انقضائه شيء آخر، أيضا حاضر . فوجب أن لا يكون هو أيضا منقسما . وهكذا القول في جميع الأجزاء الواقعة في تلك الحركة إلى آخرها . فثبت بهذا البرهان القاطع القاهر أن الحركة مركبة من أمور متتالية كل واحد منها غير قابل للقسمة البتة. وإذا ثبت هذا قلنا : وجب أن يكون الجسم أيضا كذلك، لأن القدر الذي يقطع من المسافة بالجزء الذي لا يتجزأ من الحركة إن كان منقسما كانت الحركة إلى نصفها نصف الحركة إلى آخرها . وحينئذ يكون ذلك الجزء من الحركة منقسما وقد فرضنا أنه غير منقسم. هذا خلف. وإن لم يكن منقسما فهو المطلوب. ولما كانت الحركة مركبة من أجزاء متتالية. كل واحد منها غير قابل للقسمة، وثبت أن هذا القدر المقطوع بكل واحد منهما من المسافة غير منقسم، وجب أن تكون المسافة مركبة من أجزاء متلاصقة كل واحد منها غير قابل للقسمة وهو المقصود.
The first proof: If motion is composed of successive things each of which does not accept temporal division in any way, then the body is composed of things each of which does not accept temporal division in any way. The premise is true, so the consequent is likewise. We say: motion is composed of successive things each of which does not accept temporal division, because the body is observed to move after it was not moving. This motion is an attribute additional to the essence of the body. Then we say: this attribute either does not obtain anything in the present moment, or it obtains. If nothing of it obtains in the present, it becomes impossible for it to be past or future. Because the past is what was present at some time and has now ceased. The future is what is expected to be present in some future time and has not yet been present. If it were impossible for it to have presence in any way, it would not be past, future, or present. Anything like that is non-existent entirely. So motion would have no existence at all. This is a contradiction. So it is established that something of motion must be present in the present moment. That present in the moment either accepts division in time or does not. If it accepts it, then we suppose in it two parts, one before the other, because temporal division is thus. When the first half exists, the second half is not present. When the second half comes, the first half vanishes. Then the present existent is not present in existence, rather only half of it is present. Then we repeat the first division on that half. The upshot: everything that is divided according to temporal division does not have its totality existent. And whatever has its totality present must not be divided according to temporal division. So it is established that the present of motion, what is obtained from it in the present moment, does not accept temporal division. Once this is established, we say: when that part passes away, something else also present follows its passing. So it must also be indivisible. And so on for all the parts occurring in that motion until its end. Thus it is proven by this decisive overwhelming proof that motion is composed of successive things each of which is absolutely indivisible. When this is established, we say: the body must also be like that, because the amount that is cut from the distance by the indivisible part of motion, if it were divisible, then the motion to its half would be half the motion to its end. Then that part of motion would be divisible, but we assumed it indivisible. This is a contradiction. And if it is not divisible, then it is what is sought. And since motion is composed of successive parts each indivisible, and it is established that this amount cut by each one of them from the distance is indivisible, the distance must be composed of contiguous parts each of which is indivisible. That is the intended conclusion.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage contains a full kalam proof (dalil) for the atomic composition of bodies. It is a complex argument structured in steps. First, Razi states the conditional premise: if motion is composed of successive indivisible temporal parts, then body must be composed of indivisible spatial parts. He then proves the antecedent (that motion has such parts) through a careful analysis. The proof begins by observing that motion is an attribute that becomes present after absence. This attribute must have some part present in the current moment, otherwise it would not be past or future and thus non-existent—a contradiction. That present part must be indivisible in time, because if it were divisible, then only half would be present at a time, contradicting its being wholly present. Repeating this reasoning shows all parts of motion are indivisible. Once motion is established as composed of indivisible parts, Razi shows that the distance traversed in each such part must also be indivisible, otherwise the motion part would be divisible. Thus the body (as a spatial magnitude) is composed of contiguous indivisible parts (atoms). The argument is deductive and relies on the nature of motion, time, and the actual present.

قسمة زمانية
جزء لا يتجزأ
حاضر

For motion to exist, its present part must be a temporally indivisible unit—a 'now' that does not admit further division.

What would it look like to embrace the indivisible present in your next action?

Razi argues that if nothing of motion were present at the instant, motion would be impossible. Do you live as if your actions are disconnected instants with no real presence, or do you recognize the continuous reality of your choices? How can you ensure that your deeds are truly present to Allah?
?
The proof concludes that the present part cannot be further divided. How does this challenge your daily habit of procrastination or distraction, where you treat the present as infinitely divisible? What concrete change can you make in your schedule to honor the indivisible present?

From Temporal Atoms to Spatial Atoms
Razi deduces that body is composed of indivisible spatial parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi extends the proof from indivisible temporal parts of motion to the conclusion that the body (spatial magnitude) is composed of indivisible spatial parts (atoms).

Core Idea
Motion's temporal atoms force spatial atoms.

Having established that motion is composed of successive indivisible temporal units, Razi now turns to the spatial implication. He argues that the distance traversed during each temporal unit must itself be indivisible; otherwise, the motion unit would be divisible, contradicting the previous conclusion. Thus the body is made of contiguous indivisible parts.

Guided Path
1
Review the previous conclusion
Recall that we proved motion's present part is temporally indivisible and that all parts of motion are similarly indivisible.
This is the foundation for the spatial argument.
2
Examine the transition to space
Razi says: if the distance traveled during one indivisible temporal part were divisible, then the motion to half that distance would be half the original motion, making the motion divisible.
This is a contradiction, so the distance must be indivisible.
3
Understand the conclusion
Since motion is composed of successive indivisible temporal parts, and each such part traverses an indivisible distance, the entire distance (and thus the body) must be composed of contiguous indivisible spatial parts—atoms.
This is the intended conclusion of the proof.

The first proof: If motion is composed of successive things each of which does not accept temporal division in any way, then the body is composed of things each of which does not accept temporal division in any way. The premise is true, so the consequent is likewise. We say: motion is composed of successive things each of which does not accept temporal division, because the body is observed to move after it was not moving. This motion is an attribute additional to the essence of the body. Then we say: this attribute either does not obtain anything in the present moment, or it obtains. If nothing of it obtains in the present, it becomes impossible for it to be past or future. Because the past is what was present at some time and has now ceased. The future is what is expected to be present in some future time and has not yet been present. If it were impossible for it to have presence in any way, it would not be past, future, or present. Anything like that is non-existent entirely. So motion would have no existence at all. This is a contradiction. So it is established that something of motion must be present in the present moment. That present in the moment either accepts division in time or does not. If it accepts it, then we suppose in it two parts, one before the other, because temporal division is thus. When the first half exists, the second half is not present. When the second half comes, the first half vanishes. Then the present existent is not present in existence, rather only half of it is present. Then we repeat the first division on that half. The upshot: everything that is divided according to temporal division does not have its totality existent. And whatever has its totality present must not be divided according to temporal division. So it is established that the present of motion, what is obtained from it in the present moment, does not accept temporal division. Once this is established, we say: when that part passes away, something else also present follows its passing. So it must also be indivisible. And so on for all the parts occurring in that motion until its end. Thus it is proven by this decisive overwhelming proof that motion is composed of successive things each of which is absolutely indivisible. When this is established, we say: the body must also be like that, because the amount that is cut from the distance by the indivisible part of motion, if it were divisible, then the motion to its half would be half the motion to its end. Then that part of motion would be divisible, but we assumed it indivisible. This is a contradiction. And if it is not divisible, then it is what is sought. And since motion is composed of successive parts each indivisible, and it is established that this amount cut by each one of them from the distance is indivisible, the distance must be composed of contiguous parts each of which is indivisible. That is the intended conclusion.

Commentary
This passage contains a full kalam proof (dalil) for the atomic composition of bodies. It is a complex argument structured in steps. First, Razi states the conditional premise: if motion is composed of successive indivisible temporal parts, then body must be composed of indivisible spatial parts. He then proves the antecedent (that motion has such parts) through a careful analysis. The proof begins by observing that motion is an attribute that becomes present after absence. This attribute must have some part present in the current moment, otherwise it would not be past or future and thus non-existent—a contradiction. That present part must be indivisible in time, because if it were divisible, then only half would be present at a time, contradicting its being wholly present. Repeating this reasoning shows all parts of motion are indivisible. Once motion is established as composed of indivisible parts, Razi shows that the distance traversed in each such part must also be indivisible, otherwise the motion part would be divisible. Thus the body (as a spatial magnitude) is composed of contiguous indivisible parts (atoms). The argument is deductive and relies on the nature of motion, time, and the actual present.

Fourth Proof: Line Moving on a Line
Razi gives his fourth proof that a line is composed of indivisible points.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's fourth proof that a line must be composed of indivisible points (atoms) based on the motion of a line over another line.

Core Idea
Motion across a line implies contact at points, so lines are made of indivisible points.

Razi presents another argument for atomism, this time using the motion of a line. By imagining a line moving across another line, he shows that the moving line must be composed of discrete points. This proof relies on the idea that contact occurs at a point, not over a continuum. Let's examine the passage closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The phrase 'نقطة النقطة نقطة' may appear garbled; focus on the overall argument.
2
Understand the scenario
Grasp the hypothetical: a line (L1) standing upright on another line (L2). Then L1 moves from one side of L2 to the other side.
Visualize this physical motion to see the point.
3
Follow the reasoning
Notice that as L1 moves, its parts come into contact with the stationary line L2 at points. Razi says the extremity of the moving line is a point.
The contact is discontinuous, occurring at distinct points.
4
Conclude the proof
Since the moving line contacts L2 at successive points, the moving line itself must be composed of those indivisible points. This is exactly the meaning of 'body composed of indivisible parts'.
This establishes atomism for lines.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : إذا فرضنا خطا قائما على خط ثم إن الخط القائم انتقل من أحد جانبي الخط الثاني إلى الجانب الآخر. فهذا الخط المتحرك صار بجميع الأجزاء المفترضة فيه ممسوس طرف الخط المتحرك، وطرف الخط المتحرك نقطة النقطة نقطة، فالخط المتحرك عليه وجب أن يكون مركبا من النقط التي كل واحد منها غير قابل للقسمة ولا معنى لقولنا الجسم مركب من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ إلا ذلك.
The fourth proof: If we suppose a line standing on a line, and then the standing line moves from one side of the second line to the other side, then this moving line becomes — with all its assumed parts — contiguous with the extremity of the moving line, and the extremity of the moving line is a point, point, point. So the moving line must be composed of points each of which is indivisible. And the meaning of our saying 'the body is composed of indivisible parts' is nothing other than that.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) — the fourth one — for atomism. Razi asks us to imagine a line (call it L1) standing upright on another line (L2). L1 then moves from one side of L2 to the other side. As L1 moves, each part of it comes into contact with the extremity of the moving part of L1? Actually, the text is a bit garbled: it says 'this moving line becomes — with all its assumed parts — in contact with the extremity of the moving line, and the extremity of the moving line is a point, point, point.' The idea seems to be that the moving line touches L2 at successive points along L2. Since contact occurs at a point, and the moving line passes over an infinite succession of such points, the moving line itself must be composed of those indivisible points. The final sentence states that this is exactly what is meant by 'the body is composed of indivisible parts' (al-ajza' allati la tatajazza'). Thus Razi argues that motion across a line implies that the line is made of discrete indivisible points.

Key Terms
خط
نقطة
جزء لا يتجزأ
مركب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Motion is continuous and contact is infinitely divisible.
Correction: Razi demonstrates that contact during motion occurs at discrete points, so the moving line must be composed of indivisible points.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth proof, what does the motion of a line across another line demonstrate?
A) That the moving line is indivisible.
B) That the stationary line is infinite.
C) That the line must be composed of indivisible points.
D) That motion is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Razi's fourth proof shows that motion across a line forces us to accept that lines are composed of indivisible points, supporting atomism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every motion of your body is made of indivisible points that Allah has counted, how will you answer for each moment you used your limbs in disobedience? Take a moment to recall a specific action and commit to making each 'point' of your future actions pleasing to Him.
?
Razi's proof shows that even a simple line moving has an intricate structure. Have you ever considered that your daily routine is composed of countless discrete moments? Choose one habit you do automatically—like walking or speaking—and reflect on how each tiny part of that habit is recorded. Will you use that awareness to be more mindful of your next action?
?
The proof forces you to accept that lines are composed of indivisible parts. In your spiritual life, do you often overlook small sins or small good deeds, thinking they don't matter? How can this truth about discrete parts remind you that no action is too small to be accounted for? Resolve to pay attention to the 'points' of your day.

Fifth Proof: Sphere on a Plane
Razi proves the existence of indivisible points by analyzing a sphere on a plane.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's fifth proof for atomism, which demonstrates that the contact point between a sphere and a plane must be indivisible, and that circles are composed of discrete points.

Core Idea
The contact point between sphere and plane must be indivisible, otherwise absurd consequences follow.

Razi presents a clever geometric argument to prove atomism. He considers a sphere resting on a plane and analyzes the nature of their contact. This thought experiment reveals that the contact area cannot be divisible, leading to the conclusion that space is composed of indivisible points. Let us follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the logical structure: assumption leads to contradiction.
2
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
Follow Razi's assumption that the contact point is divisible, and see the contradictions that arise: the sphere would become a plane or a polygon.
This is the core of the proof.
3
Conclude the indivisible point and the circle's composition
Notice how the proof concludes that the contact is indivisible and that a circle is made of contiguous points.
This supports atomism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : إذا وضعنا كرة حقيقية على سطح حقيقي، فموضع المماسة إما أن يكون منقسما أو لا يكون . والأول باطل وإلا لكان ذلك الموضع من الكرة منطبقا على السطح المستقيم، والمنطبق على المستقيم مستقيم فذلك الموضع من الكرة مستقيم . فإذا تدحرجت الكرة فالموضع الثاني من مواضع المماسة يكون أيضا مستقيما ثم إن موضع المماسة الثانية لا شك أنه منطبق متصل بموضع المماسة الأولى. فإن كان ذلك الاتصال على الاستقامة صارت الكرة سطحا مستويا وإن كان لا على الاستقامة، بل على الزاوية، صارت الكرة مضلعة . هذا خلف. فثبت أن موضع المماسة من الكرة شيء غير قابل للقسمة وإذا تدحرجت الكرة حتى تمت الدائرة، كانت تلك الدائرة مركبة من مواضع المماسات، وتلك المواضع نقط غير مستقيمة، فحينئذ حصلت تلك الدائرة خطا مركبا من النقط المتلاصقة . وذلك هو المطلوب.
The fifth proof: If we place a real sphere on a real plane, the place of contact is either divisible or not. The first is false, otherwise that place of the sphere would be coincident with the straight plane, and what coincides with a straight thing is straight, so that place of the sphere would be straight. Then if the sphere rolls, the second place of contact would also be straight. Then the second place of contact is undoubtedly coincident and connected to the first place of contact. If that connection is in a straight line, the sphere would become a plane surface; and if not in a straight line but at an angle, the sphere would become polygonal. This is a contradiction. So it is established that the place of contact of the sphere is something indivisible. And if the sphere rolls until it completes a circle, that circle is composed of the places of contact, and those places are non-straight points. Thus that circle becomes a line composed of contiguous points. And that is the required [conclusion].
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is the fifth proof for atomism, using a sphere on a plane. Razi states that the point of contact between a real sphere and a real plane must be either divisible or indivisible. If it were divisible, then that contact patch would be a straight line segment (since it coincides with the plane), implying the sphere's surface at that patch is straight. Then as the sphere rolls, each successive contact patch would also be straight. If these patches connect in a straight line, the sphere would become a flat plane; if they connect at an angle, the sphere would become a polygon — both absurd. Hence the contact patch must be indivisible. When the sphere rolls a full circle, the trace of contact points forms a circle. These points are 'non-straight' (i.e., they are not aligned in a straight line but curve). Therefore the circle is a line composed of contiguous indivisible points. This proves that continuous magnitudes (like a circle) are made of discrete atoms.

Key Terms
كرة
سطح
مماسة
نقطة
مركب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the contact area between a sphere and a plane is a small surface (divisible area).
Correction: Razi proves that if it were divisible, the sphere would become a plane or a polygon, which is impossible; thus the contact must be an indivisible point.

Checkpoint
What would happen if the contact place between a sphere and a plane were divisible?
A) The sphere would roll smoothly.
B) The sphere would become a plane or a polygon.
C) The sphere would not move.
D) The contact place would be a point.

Key Takeaway
Razi's sphere-on-plane proof establishes that continuous lines are composed of indivisible points, supporting atomism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the sphere's contact with the plane is indivisible, then each moment of your life's 'contact' with Allah's commands is also indivisible—a point of decision. Which point today did you treat as divisible, thinking it insignificant?
?
Razi's proof shows that the circle is composed of discrete points. Your journey towards Allah is also a path of discrete steps. Have you been careless about any step, assuming it doesn't matter? How will you now value each point of your journey?

Razi's Sixth Proof: Infinite Divisibility Leads to Actual Infinity
Razi proves that infinite divisibility implies actual infinite parts, which is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that if a body were infinitely divisible, it would contain an actual infinity of distinct points, which is impossible, and how he proves that each possible division point has a unique property forcing its actual existence.

Core Idea
Infinite potential division implies actual infinite parts — an absurdity.

Razi presents his sixth proof against the infinite divisibility of bodies. He argues that if a body could be divided infinitely, it would have to contain an actual infinity of parts — a clear absurdity. To show this, he uses the example of points on a line, each possessing a unique property that forces it to be real. Let's follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing too much, then the English translation. Let the flow of the argument sink in before we dissect it.
Notice the conditional structure: 'If ... then ... impossible, so ... impossible.'
2
Understand the first way (wajh)
Razi's first argument uses points on a line. Each possible point (like the half-cut, third-cut) has a unique property that cannot be shared. Because of this uniqueness, each point must actually exist if the line is infinitely divisible. Work through the example of the half-cut: its position is fixed; adding or subtracting a bit changes it to a different cut.
This shows that all possible division points are actually present, leading to an actual infinity.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Why does the existence of all these points imply an actual infinite? And why is that impossible? Connect to the broader theological context: bodies cannot be infinitely divisible because that would entail an actual infinity, which is rationally impossible.
The second way (wajh) is cut short but appeals to direct rational intuition that halves are distinct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : لو كان الجسم قابلا لانقسامات لا نهاية لها لكان مركبا من أجزاء لا نهاية لها بالفعل. وهذا محال، فذلك محال. بيان المقام الأول من وجهين: الأول: أن كل موضع اختص بخاصية لا تحصل في سائر المواضع، كان ذلك الموضع متميزا بالفعل عن سائر المواضع. وكل نقطة يمكن فرضها في خط، فإن تلك النقطة مختصة بخاصية ممتنعة الحصول في سائر النقط، فيلزم أن تكون كل النقط التي يمكن فرضها في الخط أن تكون حاصلة بالفعل. مقدمات هذه الحجة جلية إلا قولنا إن كل واحدة من النقط التي يمكن فرضها في الخط، فإنها تختص بخاصية لا توجد في سائر النقط التي يمكن فرضها. والدليل عليه : أن كل خط فإن مقطع النصف منه موضع معين، ويستحيل أن يكون غير تلك النقطة موضع النصف. وكذا القول في مقطع الثلث ومقطع الربع فإنك إن زدت على مقطع الثلث شيئا، أو نقصت منه شيئا، لم يكن ذلك مقطع الثلث بل مقطعا آخر وكذا القول في جميع المقاطع التي لانهاية لها . فإن لكل واحد منها موضعا لا يمكن أن يزاد عليه أو ينقص منه . فثبت أن كل نقطة فرضها في هذا الخط فإنها مختصة بخاصية يمتنع حصولها في سائر النقط الممكنة الفرض في هذا الخط . فثبت أنه لو كان الخط قابلا لانقسامات لا نهاية لها، لكانت تلك الانقسامات حاصلة فيه بالفعل. الوجه الثاني في تقرير هذه المقدمة : أنا إذا أشرنا إلى جسم بسيط، فإن صريح العقل يشهد بأن هذا النصف منه مغاير للنصف الآخر منه.
The sixth proof: If the body were susceptible to infinite divisions, it would be composed of actually infinite parts. This is impossible, so that [infinite divisibility] is impossible. An explanation of the first station [the impossibility of actual infinite] in two ways: The first: Every place that is characterized by a property not found in other places is actually distinct from other places. And every point that can be assumed in a line is characterized by a property impossible to obtain in other points, so it follows that all points that can be assumed in the line are actually present. The premises of this proof are obvious except for our statement that every one of the points that can be assumed in the line is characterized by a property not found in other points that can be assumed. The proof of that: Every line has a half-cut point that is a specific place, and it is impossible that the place of the half be other than that point. Likewise for the third-cut point and the fourth-cut point: if you add something to the third-cut or subtract something, it would not be the third-cut but another cut. And so for all cuts without end — each has a place that cannot be added to or subtracted from. So it is established that every point you assume in this line is characterized by a property impossible to obtain in other possible points in this line. So it is established that if the line were susceptible to infinite divisions, those divisions would be actually present in it. The second way of establishing this premise: If we point to a simple body, sound reason testifies that this half of it is other than the other half.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is the sixth proof against infinite divisibility, establishing that actual infinite is impossible. Razi begins with a conditional: if a body were infinitely divisible, it would be composed of actually infinite parts. That is impossible, so infinite divisibility is impossible. Then he explains the 'first station' (the impossibility of actual infinite) in two ways (wajh). The first way: any point that can be assumed in a line has a unique property (e.g., being the midpoint, third-point, etc.), so all such points must actually exist — otherwise the property would not be realized. This implies an actual infinity of points in a finite line, which is impossible. He provides a proof: every division point (half, third, quarter, etc.) has a unique, unsharable position; you cannot move it by even a jot without changing its identity. Thus each possible point is distinct and must actually exist. Therefore, if the line had infinite possible divisions, it would have actual infinite points — impossible. The second way (incomplete) appeals to sound reason: when we point to a simple body, we immediately recognize that one half is distinct from the other half, implying actual distinction of parts even without division.

Key Terms
انقسامات لا نهاية لها
أجزاء لا نهاية لها بالفعل
مقطع
خاصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Potential infinite divisibility is harmless; it does not imply any actual infinity.
Correction: Razi shows that if a body is potentially infinitely divisible, then for each possible division point there is a unique property that must actually be realized, so all those points must actually exist — an actual infinity.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi argue that every possible point on a line has a unique property?
A) Because each point is defined by its coordinates.
B) Because each cut (half, third, etc.) has a specific place that cannot be shifted.
C) Because points are indistinguishable.
D) Because the line is continuous.

Key Takeaway
Potential infinite divisibility of a line (or body) entails the actual existence of infinitely many distinct points, which is rationally impossible, so infinite divisibility is false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that a finite line cannot contain infinite potential divisions without absurdity. Your life is finite. What 'potential' distractions or actions do you keep as possibilities, assuming they are harmless because they are not actual? Which one will you actually eliminate today?
?
Razi's argument forces you to accept that every potential cut has a distinct, fixed location. Does your faith have fixed, non-negotiable truths, or do you treat them as flexible 'potentials' to be adjusted? Which truth will you commit to as absolute today?
?
If a finite body cannot sustain infinite parts, your finite heart cannot sustain infinite attachments. Which relationship or habit do you need to 'cut off' actually, not just potentially, to avoid spiritual absurdity?

Two Arguments Against the Indivisible Atom
Razi presents two proofs against the indivisible atom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the ninth and tenth proofs against the indivisible atom (the horse motion argument and the geometric boundary argument).

Core Idea
Both arguments force the indivisible atom to be divisible.

Imam Razi challenges the kalām doctrine of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard) by presenting two clever arguments. The first uses the ratio of movement to pause in a slow horse, and the second employs geometric shapes to show that any finite body must have parts of differing sizes, implying division. Let's examine each proof closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the horse argument
Follow the analogy: if slowness were due to inserted pauses, a slow horse would have more pauses than movements, but we observe no pauses, so slowness is not from pauses; thus bodies must be continuously divisible.
2
Analyze the implication for atoms
If a body were made of atoms, then in the time a fast motion covers one atom, a slow motion would cover less than an atom, which forces the atom to divide.
This is the crux of the argument.
3
Examine the geometric argument
Every finite body has boundaries. If it is a sphere, gaps between spheres are smaller than the sphere itself, so something smaller than the atom exists. If it is a polygon, angles are smaller than sides, showing parts of different sizes—hence divisibility.
The argument covers two cases: spherical and polygonal shapes.
4
Understand the conclusion
Both arguments aim to prove that the indivisible atom must be divisible, undermining the kalām position.
These are only two of ten proofs Razi mentions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سكنات هذا الفرس المذكور إلى حركاته كنسبة زيادة حركات الفلك الأعظم إلى حركات الفرس، لكن حركات الفلك أزيد من حركات هذا الفرس ألف ألف فيلزم أن يقال : سكنات هذا الفرس أزيد من حركاته ألف ألف مرة ولو كان الأمر كذلك، لما ظهرت تلك الحركات القليلة، فيما بين تلك السكنات الكثيرة، لكن الأمر بالضد؛ فإنا لا نشاهد في حركات الفرس المذكور شيئا من السكنات فعلمنا أنه ليس بطء الحركات لأجل تخلل السكنات. إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : يلزم أن يكون الجسم قابلا أبدا للقسمة؛ لأنه لو كان مركبا من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ ، فلنفرض زمانا قطعت الحركة السريعة فيه جزءا لا يتجزأ ففي ذلك الزمان إن قطع البطيء أيضا جزءا كان البطيء مثل السريع في السرعة والبطء وهذا خلف، وإن قطع البطيء أقل من جزء لزم انقسام الجوهر الفرد وهو المطلوب. الحجة العاشرة لهم كل متحيز فهو متناه، وكل متناه فإنه يحيط به حد وحدود. فإن أحاط به حد واحد فهو الكرة، وإذا تلاصقت الكرات حصلت فيما بينها فرج، بحيث يكون كل واحد من تلك الفرج أصغر من كل واحدة من تلك الكرات، فقد وجد شيء أصغر من الجوهر الفرد فينقسم الجوهر الفرد، وإن أحاط به حدود مختلفة فهو المضلعات كالمثلث والمربع، وكل ما كان كذلك فإن جانب الزاوية منه أصغر من جانب الضلع، وكل ما وقع التفاوت بالصغر والكبر في أجزائه وجوانبه، كان قابلا للانقسام، فالجوهر الفرد قابل للانقسام. فثبت أن الجوهر الفرد الذي يقول به المتكلمون لا بد أن يكون منقسما، على جميع التقديرات. ولنقتصر من دلائل نفاة الجوهر الفرد على هذه الوجوه العشرة، فإن لنا كتابا أنه قد منفردًا في هذه المسألة. ومن أراد الاستقصاء فيها فليطالع ذلك الكتاب واعلم أنا نجيب عن جميع هذه الشبه بجواب واحد ونحيل بالأجوبة المفصلة هذه الوجوه مشتركة في شيء واحد، وهو على ذلك الكتاب، فنقول : إن جميع اختص أحد جانبي الجزء بخاصية لا تحصل في الجانب الآخر منه، ولكن هذا المعنى يوجب حصول انقسامات غير متناهية بالفعل والفلاسفة لا يقولون بهذا المعنى. وما هو نتيجة هذه الشبه لا يقولون به، وما يقولون به فهو الانقسام بالقوة فقط. لا نتيجة هذه الوجوه. فثبت سقوط هذه الوجوه بأسرها. وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فهي مذكورة في الكتاب الذي صنفناه في هذه المسألة وبالله التوفيق.
The pauses of this mentioned horse to its movements are as the ratio of the increase of the movements of the greatest sphere to the movements of the horse, but the movements of the sphere exceed the movements of this horse by a thousand thousand, so it follows that the pauses of this horse exceed its movements by a thousand thousand times. If it were so, those few movements would not appear among those many pauses, but the opposite is the case; for we do not observe in the movements of the mentioned horse any pauses, so we know that the slowness of movements is not due to the interpolation of pauses. If this is established, we say: it follows that the body is always divisible; because if it were composed of indivisible parts, then let us assume a time in which the fast motion traverses an indivisible part. In that time, if the slow motion also traverses a part, then the slow would be like the fast in speed and slowness, and this is a contradiction. And if the slow traverses less than a part, then the division of the indivisible atom follows, and that is what is sought. The tenth argument for them: every occupant of space is finite, and everything finite is surrounded by a boundary and boundaries. If it is surrounded by a single boundary, it is the sphere, and when spheres are contiguous, gaps occur between them, such that each one of those gaps is smaller than each one of those spheres, so something smaller than the indivisible atom exists, so the indivisible atom divides. And if it is surrounded by different boundaries, it is the polygons like the triangle and square, and everything that is like that, the side of the angle is smaller than the side of the side, and whenever variation by smallness and largeness occurs in its parts and sides, it is divisible, so the indivisible atom is divisible. Thus it is established that the indivisible atom which the mutakallimun assert must necessarily be divisible in all estimations. And we limit ourselves from the proofs of the deniers of the indivisible atom to these ten ways, for we have a book that is [؟] separate on this question. Whoever desires thoroughness in it, let him consult that book. And know that we answer all these doubts with a single answer and refer to detailed answers [؟]. These ways share one thing, and it is [؟] that book. So we say: all [؟] the particularization of one side of the part with a property not found in the other side, but this meaning necessitates the occurrence of actual infinite divisions, and the philosophers do not affirm this meaning. And what is the result of these doubts they do not affirm, and what they affirm is only potential division, not the result of these ways. Thus the collapse of all these ways is established. As for the detailed answers, they are mentioned in the book we composed on this question, and with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage contains two arguments against the indivisible atom (jawhar fard) and a unified refutation. The first argument (lines 1-9) uses the example of a horse's motion: if slowness were due to interpolated pauses, then a very slow horse would have many pauses relative to its movements, but we observe continuous motion, so slowness is not due to pauses; thus bodies must be always divisible. The second argument (the tenth, lines 9-16) uses geometry: any extended body has boundaries; if spherical, gaps between spheres are smaller than the atom, so the atom divides; if polygonal, angles are smaller than sides, showing parts of different sizes, hence divisibility. The author then states he limits himself to these ten proofs and refers to a separate book for detail. He gives a single answer applying to all proofs: they all assume that a part can have a unique property on one side, implying actual infinite division, but the philosophers only affirm potential division, not actual. Therefore, the arguments fail. The passage concludes by noting that detailed answers are in that other book.

Key Terms
جوهر فرد (indivisible atom)
سكنات (pauses)
حركات (movements)
متحيز (occupant of space)
متناه (finite)
حد (boundary)
انقسام (division)

A) The slow motion is impossible.
B) The fast motion must also traverse less than a part.
C) The indivisible atom must divide.

Key Takeaway
Both arguments show that the assumption of indivisible atoms leads to contradictions or smaller parts, forcing divisibility.

The second argument reveals that even the smallest gaps and angles expose hidden divisibility. What about the 'small' sins or thoughts you dismiss as insignificant? Could they be the gaps through which your character is being divided? How will you address them specifically this week?
