Unified Refutation of the Ten Proofs
Razi provides a single refutation for all ten proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes all ten proofs against the indivisible atom with a single argument distinguishing actual from potential division.

Core Idea
All proofs only prove potential division, which the philosophers already accept.

Having presented ten arguments against the atom, Razi now gives a unified answer that applies to all of them. He identifies their common flaw—they assume the atom has a unique property on one side implying actual infinite division—but philosophers only affirm potential division. Therefore, the arguments fail to refute the atom.

Guided Path
1
Read the unified response
Razi states that all ten proofs share one flaw: they assume a part can have a unique property on one side, which would require actual infinite divisions.
2
Distinguish actual vs. potential division
The philosophers (falāsifa) affirm that bodies are only potentially divisible to infinity, not actually divided. The proofs only show potential division, so they do not contradict the philosophers' view.
This is the key insight.
3
Understand the conclusion
Since the arguments do not prove actual infinite division, they collapse. Razi refers to his separate book for detailed responses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سكنات هذا الفرس المذكور إلى حركاته كنسبة زيادة حركات الفلك الأعظم إلى حركات الفرس، لكن حركات الفلك أزيد من حركات هذا الفرس ألف ألف فيلزم أن يقال : سكنات هذا الفرس أزيد من حركاته ألف ألف مرة ولو كان الأمر كذلك، لما ظهرت تلك الحركات القليلة، فيما بين تلك السكنات الكثيرة، لكن الأمر بالضد؛ فإنا لا نشاهد في حركات الفرس المذكور شيئا من السكنات فعلمنا أنه ليس بطء الحركات لأجل تخلل السكنات. إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : يلزم أن يكون الجسم قابلا أبدا للقسمة؛ لأنه لو كان مركبا من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ ، فلنفرض زمانا قطعت الحركة السريعة فيه جزءا لا يتجزأ ففي ذلك الزمان إن قطع البطيء أيضا جزءا كان البطيء مثل السريع في السرعة والبطء وهذا خلف، وإن قطع البطيء أقل من جزء لزم انقسام الجوهر الفرد وهو المطلوب. الحجة العاشرة لهم كل متحيز فهو متناه، وكل متناه فإنه يحيط به حد وحدود. فإن أحاط به حد واحد فهو الكرة، وإذا تلاصقت الكرات حصلت فيما بينها فرج، بحيث يكون كل واحد من تلك الفرج أصغر من كل واحدة من تلك الكرات، فقد وجد شيء أصغر من الجوهر الفرد فينقسم الجوهر الفرد، وإن أحاط به حدود مختلفة فهو المضلعات كالمثلث والمربع، وكل ما كان كذلك فإن جانب الزاوية منه أصغر من جانب الضلع، وكل ما وقع التفاوت بالصغر والكبر في أجزائه وجوانبه، كان قابلا للانقسام، فالجوهر الفرد قابل للانقسام. فثبت أن الجوهر الفرد الذي يقول به المتكلمون لا بد أن يكون منقسما، على جميع التقديرات. ولنقتصر من دلائل نفاة الجوهر الفرد على هذه الوجوه العشرة، فإن لنا كتابا أنه قد منفردًا في هذه المسألة. ومن أراد الاستقصاء فيها فليطالع ذلك الكتاب واعلم أنا نجيب عن جميع هذه الشبه بجواب واحد ونحيل بالأجوبة المفصلة هذه الوجوه مشتركة في شيء واحد، وهو على ذلك الكتاب، فنقول : إن جميع اختص أحد جانبي الجزء بخاصية لا تحصل في الجانب الآخر منه، ولكن هذا المعنى يوجب حصول انقسامات غير متناهية بالفعل والفلاسفة لا يقولون بهذا المعنى. وما هو نتيجة هذه الشبه لا يقولون به، وما يقولون به فهو الانقسام بالقوة فقط. لا نتيجة هذه الوجوه. فثبت سقوط هذه الوجوه بأسرها. وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فهي مذكورة في الكتاب الذي صنفناه في هذه المسألة وبالله التوفيق.
The pauses of this mentioned horse to its movements are as the ratio of the increase of the movements of the greatest sphere to the movements of the horse, but the movements of the sphere exceed the movements of this horse by a thousand thousand, so it follows that the pauses of this horse exceed its movements by a thousand thousand times. If it were so, those few movements would not appear among those many pauses, but the opposite is the case; for we do not observe in the movements of the mentioned horse any pauses, so we know that the slowness of movements is not due to the interpolation of pauses. If this is established, we say: it follows that the body is always divisible; because if it were composed of indivisible parts, then let us assume a time in which the fast motion traverses an indivisible part. In that time, if the slow motion also traverses a part, then the slow would be like the fast in speed and slowness, and this is a contradiction. And if the slow traverses less than a part, then the division of the indivisible atom follows, and that is what is sought. The tenth argument for them: every occupant of space is finite, and everything finite is surrounded by a boundary and boundaries. If it is surrounded by a single boundary, it is the sphere, and when spheres are contiguous, gaps occur between them, such that each one of those gaps is smaller than each one of those spheres, so something smaller than the indivisible atom exists, so the indivisible atom divides. And if it is surrounded by different boundaries, it is the polygons like the triangle and square, and everything that is like that, the side of the angle is smaller than the side of the side, and whenever variation by smallness and largeness occurs in its parts and sides, it is divisible, so the indivisible atom is divisible. Thus it is established that the indivisible atom which the mutakallimun assert must necessarily be divisible in all estimations. And we limit ourselves from the proofs of the deniers of the indivisible atom to these ten ways, for we have a book that is [؟] separate on this question. Whoever desires thoroughness in it, let him consult that book. And know that we answer all these doubts with a single answer and refer to detailed answers [؟]. These ways share one thing, and it is [؟] that book. So we say: all [؟] the particularization of one side of the part with a property not found in the other side, but this meaning necessitates the occurrence of actual infinite divisions, and the philosophers do not affirm this meaning. And what is the result of these doubts they do not affirm, and what they affirm is only potential division, not the result of these ways. Thus the collapse of all these ways is established. As for the detailed answers, they are mentioned in the book we composed on this question, and with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage contains two arguments against the indivisible atom (jawhar fard) and a unified refutation. The first argument (lines 1-9) uses the example of a horse's motion: if slowness were due to interpolated pauses, then a very slow horse would have many pauses relative to its movements, but we observe continuous motion, so slowness is not due to pauses; thus bodies must be always divisible. The second argument (the tenth, lines 9-16) uses geometry: any extended body has boundaries; if spherical, gaps between spheres are smaller than the atom, so the atom divides; if polygonal, angles are smaller than sides, showing parts of different sizes, hence divisibility. The author then states he limits himself to these ten proofs and refers to a separate book for detail. He gives a single answer applying to all proofs: they all assume that a part can have a unique property on one side, implying actual infinite division, but the philosophers only affirm potential division, not actual. Therefore, the arguments fail. The passage concludes by noting that detailed answers are in that other book.

Key Terms
فلاسفة (philosophers)
انقسام بالفعل (actual division)
انقسام بالقوة (potential division)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The ten proofs demonstrate that the atom is actually divisible into an infinite number of parts.
Correction: The proofs only demonstrate potential divisibility, which the philosophers already accept. They do not prove actual infinite division.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's unified refutation, what do all ten proofs incorrectly assume that leads to actual infinite division?
A) That the atom is spherical.
B) That one side of the atom has a unique property not found on the other side.
C) That the atom is subject to motion.
D) That the atom is composed of smaller parts.

Key Takeaway
Razi refutes all ten arguments by showing they rely on actual infinite division, which the philosophers do not hold; only potential division is admitted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are faced with multiple objections to a truth you hold, do you tend to address each one individually, or do you seek the underlying assumption they all share? How would Razi's approach change the way you defend your beliefs?
?
The philosophers only accepted potential division, yet Razi treated this as a victory. Are there areas in your life where you have been satisfied with a 'potential' commitment rather than an actual one? What would it look like to move from potential to actual in your relationship with Allah?
?
Think of a criticism of your faith that once troubled you. Did it rely on a misunderstanding of what you actually believe? How can Razi's unified refutation inspire you to clarify the real point of contention and respond with precision?

Soul as Four Humors: Correlation Does Not Prove Causation
Razi presents and refutes the humoral theory of the soul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Razi dismisses the humoral theory of the soul as weak due to the insufficiency of correlation (dawarān) to establish causation.

Core Idea
Correlation does not prove causation—a key logical principle in kalam.

Imam Razi continues his survey of historical views on the soul by presenting the fourth view: the soul is the balanced mixture of four humors. The proponents argue from observed correlation, but Razi points out a fundamental logical flaw. This lesson unpacks that flaw and its significance for theological methodology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal English translation. Notice the structure: the view, the proof, and the refutation.
2
Identify the claim, evidence, and refutation
The passage has three parts: (1) the definition of the soul as the total of four humors with specific quantity, (2) the proponents' proof from correlation, and (3) Razi's refutation that correlation does not prove causality.
3
Reflect on the logical principle
Consider why correlation (dawarān) is insufficient for certainty. Could there be an underlying cause that is not the humors themselves? This is a key lesson in causal reasoning.
This principle applies beyond this specific view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورابعها أن النفس عبارة عن مجموع الأخلاط الأربعة، بشرط أن يكون لكل واحد منها مقدار معين. واحتجوا عليه بأنه مهما كانت هذه الأخلاط الأربعة باقية على كمياتها المخصوصة وكيفياتها المخصوصة، كانت الحياة باقية ومهما لم تبق تلك الكميات وتلك الكيفيات، زالت الحياة وهذا الدليل ضعيف؛ لأن الدوران لا يفيد العلم بالعلية
And the fourth: that the soul is the total of the four humors (akhlāṭ), on condition that each of them has a specific quantity. They argued for it by saying that whenever these four humors remain in their specific quantities and qualities, life remains, and whenever those quantities and qualities do not remain, life vanishes. And this proof is weak, because correlation (dawarān) does not provide knowledge of causality.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth sub-view: the soul is the combination of the four humors (blood, phlegm, yellow bile, black bile) in a precise balance. The proponents argue by correlation: when the humors are balanced, life is present; when they are imbalanced, life ceases. Razi dismisses this as weak because mere correlation (dawarān) does not prove causation. Life could be caused by something else that coincides with the humoral balance, not by the humors themselves.

Key Terms
أخلاط أربعة (akhlāṭ arbaʿa)
كمية (kammiyya)
كيفية (kayfiyya)
دوران (dawarān)
علية (ʿilliyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that if two things are always observed together, one must cause the other.
Correction: Razi points out that correlation (dawarān) is insufficient to prove causation; a hidden third factor could be the true cause.

Checkpoint
What logical flaw does Razi identify in the humors theory of the soul?
A) It relies on revelation
B) It uses correlation (dawarān) which does not prove causation
C) It denies the existence of the soul
D) It contradicts the Quran

Key Takeaway
Razi shows that the mere correlation between humoral balance and life does not prove that the soul is composed of humors; causality requires a stronger demonstration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that because something always happens after another, the first causes the second? How might this lesson change the way you evaluate your own beliefs about cause and effect in your daily life?
?
Razi points out that correlation does not give certain knowledge of causality. In your own life, what is a belief you hold that is based on repeated correlation rather than true proof? Will you continue to hold it, and why?
?
This lesson teaches that a weak argument can be confidently presented. What weak arguments do you rely on to justify your spiritual or moral choices? Are you willing to examine them with the same logical rigor Razi applies?

Defining Void and the Philosophers' Stance
Al-Razi defines void and states the philosophical consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of void (al-khala') as described by al-Razi and know which philosophers affirmed or denied its existence within the world.

Core Idea
Void is defined as two bodies not touching without anything between them; most philosophers deny it, but Abu al-Barakat affirms it.

Al-Razi begins this problem by providing a precise definition of 'void' and then notes the position of the majority of philosophers. Understanding this background is essential for the logical argument that follows, as it sets up the conceptual foundation of the debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of void
Read the Arabic passage that defines void. Notice that it requires two bodies not touching and nothing between them that touches them.
This is a technical definition, not just empty space.
2
Note the positions of philosophers
Al-Razi states that most philosophers deny void within the world, except Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi who affirms it. Consider why such a debate might matter.
This sets up the need for a proof.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why would denying or affirming void affect other philosophical or theological claims? This background frames the argument to come.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة التاسعة والعشرون في إثبات الخلاء اعلم : أن معنى الخلاء هو أن يوجد جسمان لا يتماسان ولا يوجد بينهما ما يمساسه وأكثر الفلاسفة ينكرون الخلاء داخل العالم، إلا أبا البركات البغدادي فإنه يثبته وأقوى ما قيل في إثبات الخلاء وجهان: الحجة الأولى: أن الجسم إذا انتقل من مكان إلى مكان فالمنتقل إليه إما أن يقال : إنه كان خاليا قبل انتقال هذا المنتقل إليه، أو كان مملوءًا، فإن قلنا : إنه كان خاليًا فقد ثبت القول بالخلاء وإن قلنا : إنه كان مملوءًا فعندما انتقل هذا الجسم إليه إما أن يقال : إنه بقي ذلك الجسم فيه أو انتقل ذلك الجسم من ذلك المكان إلى مكان آخر، فإن بقي ذلك الجسم فيه حال ما انتقل إليه هذا الجسم، لزم اجتماع الجسمين في مكان واحد وهو محال وإن انتقل ذلك الجسم عن ذلك المكان فإما أن يقال : إنه انتقل إلى مكان ذلك الجسم الذي انتقل إلى مكانه أو إلى مكان آخر فإن كان الأول لزم الدور؛ لأن هذا لا يمكنه الانتقال عن مكانه إلا إذا فرغ المكان عن الثاني، ولن يفرغ المكان من الثاني إلا إذا فرغ المكان الأول عن الجسم الأول. وما أفضى إلى الدور امتنع وجوده. وأما إن انتقل إلى مكان آخر عاد التقسيم الأول فيه ويلزم أن يقال : مهما تحركت البقة أو النملة، لزم أن يتحرك جملة عالم الأجسام، وذلك محال فثبت أن القول بعدم الخلاء يفضي إلى أقسام باطلة، فيكون القول بعدم الخلاء باطلا، فيكون القول بالخلاء حقا. فإن قيل : فعلى هذا التقدير يلزمكم أن تقولوا : إذا تحركت الذرة في قعر البحر المحيط أن تندفع كلية ذلك البحر، أو تثبتها في داخل الماء أحيازا خالية وذلك بعيد لأن الماء جرم ثقيل سيال، وإذا وجد موضعا خاليا، سال إليه بالطبع قلنا الخلاء داخل ماء البحر غير بعيد - لأن عندنا خالق العالم فاعل مختار، ولا يبعد أن يمنع أجرام الماء عن السيلان إلى تلك الأحياز الفارغة إلا أن القائل أن يقول : لم
The Twenty-Ninth Problem: On the existence of void. Know that the meaning of void is that two bodies exist that do not touch each other and there is nothing between them that touches them. And most philosophers deny void within the world, except Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi, for he affirms it. And the strongest arguments given for the existence of void are two: The first argument: that when a body moves from one place to another, the destination is either said to have been empty before the arrival of this moving body, or filled. If we say it was empty, then the affirmation of void is established. And if we say it was filled, then when this body moves to it, either that body remains in it or that body moves from that place to another. If that body remains in it at the time this body moves into it, then two bodies occupying one place would be necessary, and that is impossible. And if that body moves from that place, then either it moves to the place of the body that moved into its place, or to another place. If the first, then circularity is necessary, because this one cannot move from its place unless the place is vacated of the second, and the place will only be vacated of the second if the first place is vacated of the first body. And whatever leads to circularity is impossible to exist. And if it moves to another place, the first division recurs concerning it, and it would be necessary to say that whenever a gnat or an ant moves, it would necessitate the motion of the entire world of bodies, and that is impossible. So it is established that the denial of void leads to false divisions, therefore the denial of void is false, therefore the affirmation of void is true. If it is said: According to this estimation, you would have to say that if an atom moves at the bottom of the encompassing sea, it would push the whole of that sea, or you would establish empty spaces inside the water, and that is far-fetched because water is a heavy fluid substance, and if it finds an empty place, it naturally flows into it. We say: Void inside the water of the sea is not far-fetched, because our Creator is a free agent, and it is not improbable that He prevents the bodies of water from flowing into those empty spaces, except that the objector may say: Why
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a new problem (المسألة التاسعة والعشرون) on proving void (al-khala'). Al-Razi defines void as two bodies not touching with nothing between them that touches them. He notes that most philosophers deny void within the world, except Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi. Then he presents the strongest argument (two sides, but only one is detailed). The argument proceeds by considering the motion of a body from one place to another. The destination is either empty or filled. If empty, void is proven. If filled, the occupying body either stays (impossible: two bodies in one place) or moves. If it moves, it either goes to the original body's previous place (leading to circularity) or to another place, leading to an infinite regress such that every motion of a gnat would require the motion of the entire universe. Since these consequences are false, the denial of void is false, so void must exist. Then an objection (فإن قيل) is raised: if this argument is accepted, then if a tiny particle moves at the bottom of the ocean, it would either push the entire ocean or create empty spaces in the water, which is unlikely because water is heavy and fluid and would naturally flow into any empty space. The answer (قلنا) appeals to divine omnipotence: the Creator is a free agent (fa'il mukhtar) who can prevent water from flowing into those empty spaces. The answer is cut off at the bottom of the page.

Key Terms
الخلاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the definition of void according to al-Razi?
A) An empty space with no bodies whatsoever.
B) Two bodies not touching with nothing between them that touches them.
C) A vacuum inside water.
D) A place where nothing exists.

Key Takeaway
Void is not simply emptiness but a specific condition between two bodies, and most philosophers deny it within the world.

?
The philosophers denied void inside the world based on assumptions. What assumptions about the universe have you inherited without questioning? Are you ready to examine them in light of revelation?

Proof of Void from Motion and Divine Power
Al-Razi presents the first proof for void from motion and answers an objection about water and divine power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's main argument for the existence of void based on motion and how he answers an objection regarding water and divine power.

Core Idea
Denying void leads to absurd consequences like infinite regress or universal motion, so void must exist.

Al-Razi now presents the strongest argument for void, which proceeds by analyzing what happens when a body moves to a new location. He shows that without void, impossible consequences follow. He then addresses an objection about water filling empty spaces, appealing to Allah's power as a free agent.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage that contains the first argument. Pay attention to the logical steps and the two possibilities considered.
The argument is a dilemma: destination empty or filled.
2
Identify the logical steps
If destination is empty → void proven. If filled → either occupying body stays (impossible) or moves. If it moves → circularity or infinite regress leading to absurdity.
Each step is designed to force acceptance of void.
3
Understand the objection
The objector says this argument would require either pushing the entire sea or creating voids in water, but water naturally flows to fill voids. Consider why this is a challenge.
The objection relies on natural properties of water.
4
Note al-Razi's answer
Al-Razi answers by invoking divine omnipotence: Allah, as a free agent, can prevent water from flowing. Reflect on the role of God's power in this argument.
This shows the theological dimension of the debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة التاسعة والعشرون في إثبات الخلاء اعلم : أن معنى الخلاء هو أن يوجد جسمان لا يتماسان ولا يوجد بينهما ما يمساسه وأكثر الفلاسفة ينكرون الخلاء داخل العالم، إلا أبا البركات البغدادي فإنه يثبته وأقوى ما قيل في إثبات الخلاء وجهان: الحجة الأولى: أن الجسم إذا انتقل من مكان إلى مكان فالمنتقل إليه إما أن يقال : إنه كان خاليا قبل انتقال هذا المنتقل إليه، أو كان مملوءًا، فإن قلنا : إنه كان خاليًا فقد ثبت القول بالخلاء وإن قلنا : إنه كان مملوءًا فعندما انتقل هذا الجسم إليه إما أن يقال : إنه بقي ذلك الجسم فيه أو انتقل ذلك الجسم من ذلك المكان إلى مكان آخر، فإن بقي ذلك الجسم فيه حال ما انتقل إليه هذا الجسم، لزم اجتماع الجسمين في مكان واحد وهو محال وإن انتقل ذلك الجسم عن ذلك المكان فإما أن يقال : إنه انتقل إلى مكان ذلك الجسم الذي انتقل إلى مكانه أو إلى مكان آخر فإن كان الأول لزم الدور؛ لأن هذا لا يمكنه الانتقال عن مكانه إلا إذا فرغ المكان عن الثاني، ولن يفرغ المكان من الثاني إلا إذا فرغ المكان الأول عن الجسم الأول. وما أفضى إلى الدور امتنع وجوده. وأما إن انتقل إلى مكان آخر عاد التقسيم الأول فيه ويلزم أن يقال : مهما تحركت البقة أو النملة، لزم أن يتحرك جملة عالم الأجسام، وذلك محال فثبت أن القول بعدم الخلاء يفضي إلى أقسام باطلة، فيكون القول بعدم الخلاء باطلا، فيكون القول بالخلاء حقا. فإن قيل : فعلى هذا التقدير يلزمكم أن تقولوا : إذا تحركت الذرة في قعر البحر المحيط أن تندفع كلية ذلك البحر، أو تثبتها في داخل الماء أحيازا خالية وذلك بعيد لأن الماء جرم ثقيل سيال، وإذا وجد موضعا خاليا، سال إليه بالطبع قلنا الخلاء داخل ماء البحر غير بعيد - لأن عندنا خالق العالم فاعل مختار، ولا يبعد أن يمنع أجرام الماء عن السيلان إلى تلك الأحياز الفارغة إلا أن القائل أن يقول : لم
The Twenty-Ninth Problem: On the existence of void. Know that the meaning of void is that two bodies exist that do not touch each other and there is nothing between them that touches them. And most philosophers deny void within the world, except Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi, for he affirms it. And the strongest arguments given for the existence of void are two: The first argument: that when a body moves from one place to another, the destination is either said to have been empty before the arrival of this moving body, or filled. If we say it was empty, then the affirmation of void is established. And if we say it was filled, then when this body moves to it, either that body remains in it or that body moves from that place to another. If that body remains in it at the time this body moves into it, then two bodies occupying one place would be necessary, and that is impossible. And if that body moves from that place, then either it moves to the place of the body that moved into its place, or to another place. If the first, then circularity is necessary, because this one cannot move from its place unless the place is vacated of the second, and the place will only be vacated of the second if the first place is vacated of the first body. And whatever leads to circularity is impossible to exist. And if it moves to another place, the first division recurs concerning it, and it would be necessary to say that whenever a gnat or an ant moves, it would necessitate the motion of the entire world of bodies, and that is impossible. So it is established that the denial of void leads to false divisions, therefore the denial of void is false, therefore the affirmation of void is true. If it is said: According to this estimation, you would have to say that if an atom moves at the bottom of the encompassing sea, it would push the whole of that sea, or you would establish empty spaces inside the water, and that is far-fetched because water is a heavy fluid substance, and if it finds an empty place, it naturally flows into it. We say: Void inside the water of the sea is not far-fetched, because our Creator is a free agent, and it is not improbable that He prevents the bodies of water from flowing into those empty spaces, except that the objector may say: Why
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a new problem (المسألة التاسعة والعشرون) on proving void (al-khala'). Al-Razi defines void as two bodies not touching with nothing between them that touches them. He notes that most philosophers deny void within the world, except Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi. Then he presents the strongest argument (two sides, but only one is detailed). The argument proceeds by considering the motion of a body from one place to another. The destination is either empty or filled. If empty, void is proven. If filled, the occupying body either stays (impossible: two bodies in one place) or moves. If it moves, it either goes to the original body's previous place (leading to circularity) or to another place, leading to an infinite regress such that every motion of a gnat would require the motion of the entire universe. Since these consequences are false, the denial of void is false, so void must exist. Then an objection (فإن قيل) is raised: if this argument is accepted, then if a tiny particle moves at the bottom of the ocean, it would either push the entire ocean or create empty spaces in the water, which is unlikely because water is heavy and fluid and would naturally flow into any empty space. The answer (قلنا) appeals to divine omnipotence: the Creator is a free agent (fa'il mukhtar) who can prevent water from flowing into those empty spaces. The answer is cut off at the bottom of the page.

Key Terms
الخلاء
الدور
الفاعل المختار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument for void relies on physical observation or empirical evidence.
Correction: Al-Razi's argument is purely logical, based on the impossibility of two bodies in one place and the absurd consequences of denying void. The objection and answer show that even if natural laws seem to oppose void, divine power can override them.

Checkpoint
What does al-Razi claim would happen if void is denied and a gnat moves?
A) The whole universe would move.
B) The gnat would be crushed.
C) The air would compress.
D) Time would stop.

Key Takeaway
Denying void leads to absurdities, so void must exist; even if natural laws seem to oppose it, God's power can sustain it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When faced with a logical proof that contradicts your intuition, as Al-Razi's proof for void might, do you submit to reason or cling to your initial impression? What does your response reveal about your commitment to truth in matters of aqeedah?
?
Al-Razi argues that God can prevent water from flowing into a void. Do you truly believe that Allah's power extends to suspending all natural laws, even those you experience daily? How does this belief shape your reliance on Him in moments of crisis?
?
The proof shows that denying void leads to absurdities. In your own life, are there beliefs you hold that, if followed to their logical end, result in contradictions? Will you have the courage to abandon them for the truth, as Al-Razi demands consistency?

First Argument for the Existence of Void with Objection and Reply
Al-Razi presents the first argument for the void, then answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's first logical argument for the existence of void and how occasionalist theology addresses objections to it.

Core Idea
If void didn't exist, every movement would be impossible or absurd.

Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi begins his discussion of the void (al-khala') by presenting a rigorous logical proof based on the impossibility of co-location and circularity. This passage demonstrates the dialectical method of kalam: a dilemma is posed, its absurd consequences are drawn, and then an objection and occasionalist reply are examined. Although the argument may seem abstract, it grounds key theological commitments about divine power and creation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
The argument starts with a simple observation: when a body moves, its destination must be either empty or filled. These two options form the basis of the proof.
Note that 'empty' here means void.
2
Trace the 'filled' branch
If the destination is filled, the occupying body either remains (impossible co-location) or moves. Follow the reasoning for the moving option.
3
Identify circularity and infinite regress
If the occupying body moves to the original body's place, circularity occurs. If it moves elsewhere, an infinite regress of movements would result, requiring all bodies to move with any small motion.
4
Examine the objection and reply
The objector challenges the proof by pointing out that water naturally flows into empty spaces, making void in water impossible. Al-Razi responds by invoking God's power to prevent natural flow, then the objector proposes an alternative occasionalist explanation that would invalidate the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الأولى: أن الجسم إذا انتقل من مكان إلى مكان فالمنتقل إليه إما أن يقال : إنه كان خاليا قبل انتقال هذا المنتقل إليه، أو كان مملوءًا، فإن قلنا : إنه كان خاليًا فقد ثبت القول بالخلاء وإن قلنا : إنه كان مملوءًا فعندما انتقل هذا الجسم إليه إما أن يقال : إنه بقي ذلك الجسم فيه أو انتقل ذلك الجسم من ذلك المكان إلى مكان آخر، فإن بقي ذلك الجسم فيه حال ما انتقل إليه هذا الجسم، لزم اجتماع الجسمين في مكان واحد وهو محال وإن انتقل ذلك الجسم عن ذلك المكان فإما . أن يقال : إنه انتقل إلى مكان ذلك الجسم الذي انتقل إلى مكانه أو إلى مكان آخر فإن كان الأول لزم الدور؛ لأن هذا لا يمكنه الانتقال عن مكانه إلا إذا فرغ المكان عن الثاني، ولن يفرغ المكان من الثاني إلا إذا فرغ المكان الأول عن الجسم الأول. وما أفضي إلى الدور امتنع وجوده. وأما إن انتقل إلى مكان آخر عاد التقسيم الأول فيه ويلزم أن يقال : مهما تحركت البقة أو النملة، لزم أن يتحرك جملة عالم الأجسام، وذلك محال فثبت أن القول بعدم الخلاء يفضي إلى أقسام باطلة، فيكون القول بعدم الخلاء باطلا، فيكون القول بالخلاء حقا. فإن قيل : فعلى هذا التقدير يلزمكم أن تقولوا : إذا تحركت الذرة في قعر البحر المحيط أن تندفع كلية ذلك البحر، أو تثبتها في داخل الماء أحيازا خالية وذلك بعيد لأن الماء جرم ثقيل سيال، وإذا وجد موضعا خاليا، سال إليه بالطبع قلنا الخلاء داخل ماء البحر غير بعيد - لأن عندنا خالق العالم فاعل مختار، ولا يبعد أن يمنع أجرام الماء عن السيلان إلى تلك الأحياز الفارغة إلا أن القائل أن يقول : لم لا يجوز أن يقال العالم كله ملآن إلا أن الجسم إذا انتقل من مكان إلى مكان فإن الفاعل المختار بعدم الجسم الذي كان حاصلا في المكان المنتقل إليه، ويخلق جسما المكان المستقل فيه، وعلى هذا التقدير يسقط دليلكم
The first proof: When a body moves from one place to another, the destination is either said to have been empty before the movement of this moving body, or it was filled. If we say it was empty, then the claim of void is established. If we say it was filled, then when this body moved to it, either that body remained in it or that body moved from that place to another. If it remained in it at the time when this body moved to it, then two bodies would necessarily occupy a single place, which is impossible. If that body moved from that place, then it is said either it moved to the place of the body that moved to its place, or to another place. If the first, circularity (al-dawar) follows, because this cannot move from its place unless the place is empty of the second, and the place will not become empty of the second unless the first place becomes empty of the first body. Whatever leads to circularity is impossible. If it moves to another place, the same division applies to it, and it would necessitate that whenever a flea or an ant moves, the entire world of bodies would have to move, which is impossible. Therefore, the denial of void leads to false consequences, so the denial of void is false, and the affirmation of void is true. If it is said: According to this reasoning, you are forced to say that if an atom moves in the bottom of the encompassing sea, the entirety of that sea would be displaced, or you would have to admit empty spaces within the water, which is far-fetched because water is a heavy liquid, and if it finds an empty space, it naturally flows into it. We say: The void within the water of the sea is not far-fetched, because we have a Creator of the world who is an agent with free will, and it is not improbable that He prevents the water bodies from flowing into those empty spaces. However, the objector may say: Why is it not allowed to say that the entire world is filled, but when a body moves from one place to another, the free agent annihilates the body that was present in the destination and creates a body in the place from which it moved? On this estimation, your proof collapses.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof for the existence of void, structured as a dilemma. The argument begins by considering the movement of a body from one location to another. If the destination is empty before movement, then void exists. If it is filled, then either the occupying body remains (causing two bodies in one place, impossible) or it moves. If it moves, it either goes to the original body's vacated place (circularity) or to another place, which leads to an infinite regress of movements affecting all bodies, an absurdity. Hence, void must be affirmed. Then an objection is raised: If the void is accepted in water, it contradicts natural flow. Al-Razi responds that God's power can prevent natural flow, invoking occasionalism. The objector then proposes an alternative: God annihilates and creates bodies to avoid void, which would invalidate the proof. Al-Razi leaves this as a challenge.

Key Terms
الخلاء (al-khala')
الدور (circularity)
الفاعل المختار (free agent/voluntary agent)
بعد/إعدام (annihilation/creation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument for void is based on empirical observation of movement.
Correction: The argument is a logical proof based on the impossibility of two bodies in one place and circularity, not on empirical measurement or physics.

Checkpoint
What does al-Razi conclude if the destination of a moving body is already occupied and the occupying body moves to the original body's place?
A) This is possible and proves void.
B) This leads to circularity, which is impossible.
C) This leads to two bodies in one place.
D) This is the only consistent option.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi demonstrates that denying void leads to impossible consequences (co-location, circularity, infinite regress), while affirming void avoids them, supported by occasionalist theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument forces you to choose: either the universe contains void, or God is constantly annihilating and recreating bodies at every moment. Which description makes you feel God's power more directly in your daily life? Commit to one specific moment today where you will consciously attribute a physical event (like your heartbeat or a falling leaf) to God's direct action, not natural law alone.
?
Al-Razi's opponent offered an alternative where God directly controls every movement without void. In your own life, do you live as if God directly controls every outcome, or do you rely on 'natural' causes as if they are independent of Him? Where do you most need to submit your trust in physical causality to God's absolute sovereignty? Write one area you will actively work on this week.
?
The argument uses logic to prove something unseen (void). When have you trusted your own reasoning about God over what He has revealed in the Qur'an? How does this lesson challenge you to prioritize revelation even when human logic seems compelling?

Second Argument for Void from Two Surfaces
Al-Razi presents the second proof for void using two perfectly flat surfaces and their separation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's second argument for void, which relies on the conceptual possibility of perfectly planar surfaces and the logical necessity of void upon their separation.

Core Idea
Conceptual possibility of perfect surfaces proves void is necessary.

Al-Razi presents a sophisticated a priori argument for the existence of void. By imagining two perfectly flat surfaces in full contact and then separating them, he argues that a void must appear between them. This lesson walks through his four premises, from the possibility of such surfaces to the necessity of void, even though the text is incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the structure of premises and the logical flow.
The passage is incomplete; we have only part of the fourth premise.
2
Identify the four premises
The argument is built on four premises. Find each one and understand what it claims.
The first two are about possibility, the third about possibility of separation, the fourth about the conclusion.
3
Analyze the proof for each premise
For each premise, examine how al-Razi proves it. Note the use of concepts like infinite regress, composition from points, and contact.
The first premise uses a reduction to planar surfaces to avoid infinite regress.
4
Understand the necessity of void
Even though the passage is cut off, grasp that al-Razi argues any body that could fill the gap must come from outside or pores, both leading to a moment of emptiness.
The completion of the refutation of the pores objection is missing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية في إثبات الخلاء : أنا إذا فرضنا سطحين مستويين انطبق أحدهما بتمامه على الآخر، ثم إذا فرضنا ارتفاع أحدهما عن الآخر دفعة، فعند هذا يلزم القطع بحصول الخلاء فيما بين ذينك الجسمين . وههنا مقدمات : المقدمة الأولى : أنه يمكن فرض سطحين مستويين من كل الوجوه ويدل على إمكانه : أن عدم الاستواء في السطح. إما أن يكون بسبب اختلاف أجزائه في الارتفاع والانخفاض، أو بسبب حصول المسام فيه أما الأول فلا بد وأن يكون بسبب سطوح صغار يتصل بعضها ببعض، لا على الاستقامة، بل على الزاوية ولا بد الانتهاء إلى سطوح صغار مستوية، وإلا لذهبت الزوايا إلى غير النهاية وهو محال، وأما حصول المسام في أجزاء السطح فهذا لو حصل فلا بد أن يحصل بين كل منقذين سطح متصل، وإلا لزم كون السطح مركبا من نقط متباينة وذلك محال فوجب القطع بوجود سطوح مستوية. وأما المقدمة الثانية : وهي أنه يجوز وجود سطحين مستويين يتماسان بالكلية فهذا ظاهر. لأن تماس بعض جوانب السطوح ممكن فيكون تماسها أيضا بالكلية ممكنا ؛ لأن جميع الأجزاء المفروضة في السطح الواحد متساوية، وما صح على البعض جاز على الباقي. وأما المقدمة الثالثة وهي أن ارتفاع أحد السطحين بكليته عن السطح الآخر ممكن فبرهانه أن أحد السطحين لما كان بكليته مماسا للسطح الآخر فإذا ارتفع أحد أجزائه عما تحته فالجزء المتصل يجب أيضا أن يرتفع عما تحته. وإلا لزم وقوع التفكك في السطح الأعلى وهو محال. وأما المقدمة الرابعة - وهي أنه إذا حصلت هذه الأمور، لزم وقوع الخلاء : فيما بين هذين السطحين - وذلك لأنه لو حصل جسم فيما بينهما لكان ذلك الجسم إما أن ينتقل من الخارج إليه أو يحصل من مسام السطح الأعلى والأسفل. فإن انتقل من الخارج إلى ذلك الوسط فحينما يكون ذلك الجسم المنتقل حاصلا في الطرفين لا يكون حاصلا في الوسط ففي ذلك الوقت يكون الوسط خاليا وهو المطلوب. وأما القول بأنه يوجد من مسام الأعلى والأسفل. فهذا أيضا باطل لأنا
The second proof for the existence of void: If we suppose two perfectly planar surfaces, one completely overlaying the other, and then suppose one of them rises from the other all at once, then it would necessarily follow that void occurs between these two bodies. Here there are premises: The first premise: It is possible to suppose two perfectly planar surfaces from all aspects. Proof of its possibility: Non-planarity in a surface is either due to differences in its parts in elevation and depression, or due to the presence of pores. As for the first, it must be due to small planar surfaces connected to each other not in a straight line but at an angle, and it must lead to a final set of planar surfaces, otherwise angles would go to infinity, which is impossible. As for the presence of pores in the parts of the surface, if they occur, then there must be a continuous surface between every two pores, otherwise the surface would be composed of discrete points, which is impossible. Therefore, the existence of planar surfaces is certain. The second premise: It is permissible for two planar surfaces to be in complete contact. This is obvious, because contact of some parts of surfaces is possible, so complete contact is also possible, because all supposed parts in a single surface are equal, and what is valid for some is permissible for the rest. The third premise: It is possible for one surface to rise completely from the other. Its proof: Since one surface is in complete contact with the other, if one of its parts rises from what is below it, then the connected part must also rise from what is below it, otherwise separation (tafakkuk) in the upper surface would occur, which is impossible. The fourth premise: If these things occur, then void necessarily occurs between these two surfaces. This is because if a body were to exist between them, that body either would have to transfer from outside into that space or come from the pores of the upper and lower surfaces. If it transfers from outside to that intermediate space, then at the moment when that transferring body is at the two ends, it is not present in the middle, so at that time the middle is empty, which is what is desired. As for the claim that it comes from the pores of the upper and lower surfaces, this is also false because we...
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for void, which proceeds through four premises. The argument imagines two perfectly flat surfaces in full contact, then one lifts off. Al-Razi first proves it is possible to conceive such surfaces by analyzing non-planarity down to irreducible planar parts and rejecting infinite regress or composition from points. Second, complete contact between two planar surfaces is possible since partial contact is possible and parts are homogeneous. Third, one surface can rise completely without disintegrating. Fourth, when these conditions hold, a void must appear between them because any intermediate body would have to either come from outside (leaving the middle briefly empty) or emerge from pores—which he argues is false, though the text cuts off. This argument relies on a priori conceptual possibility rather than empirical observation.

Key Terms
سطح
مسطح مستو
تماس
ارتفاع
مسام
تفكك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument requires that perfectly planar surfaces actually exist in the physical world.
Correction: Al-Razi only needs them to be conceptually possible; the argument is a priori and does not depend on empirical existence.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi's second argument, what must occur if two perfectly flat surfaces in complete contact are separated all at once?
A) They will remain in contact at some points.
B) A void must exist between them.
C) Air will rush in from the pores.
D) The surfaces will disintegrate.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's second argument demonstrates that the existence of void is logically necessitated by the conceptual possibility of perfect planar surfaces and their separation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Razi argues that void is a logical necessity from the possibility of two surfaces separating. Where in your own life have you assumed something is impossible simply because you cannot observe it directly? Will you now reconsider what rational necessity demands, even when your senses cannot confirm it?

?
The argument forces you to accept a conclusion that contradicts everyday experience (that space can be empty of body). What beliefs do you hold today that are contradicted by your daily experience but are logically necessary? Are you willing to follow reason where it leads, even if it unsettles you?

The Islamic Theologians' Objection: Void Averted by Divine Creation
Razi states the Islamic theologians' objection based on divine creative power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic theologians challenged the proof for void by appealing to God's creative power as a free agent.

Core Idea
God's power to create instantly renders void unnecessary.

Imam Razi presents an objection from Islamic theologians against the philosophical proof for the existence of void. While the proof is logically sound on its own premises, it fails to account for the free action of the Creator. The objection shows that if God can create a body at the moment of separation, void never occurs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how Razi distinguishes between philosophers and Islamic theologians.
2
Identify the two principles
The passage contrasts the principles of philosophers (who deny a free creator) with those of Islamic theologians (who affirm a free agent). Note that the objection only arises on the latter.
3
Understand the objection
The objection asks: why cannot the free agent create a body at the very instant the surfaces separate? If He does, void never occurs. Grasp the logic: the possibility of divine creation blocks the necessity of void.
4
Reflect on the implication
This objection does not prove void impossible, only that the proof fails under Islamic theological principles. Reflect on the role of divine power in arguments about the natural world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن هذه الحجة لا يمكن الجواب عنها على أصول الفلاسفة، إلا أن على أصول الإسلاميين عليها سؤال. وهو أن يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن في أول وقت رفع أحد السطحين عن الآخر، يخلق الفاعل المختار فيما بينهما جسما؟ وعلى هذا التقدير لا يحصل الخلاء البتة.
And know that this argument cannot be answered upon the principles of the philosophers, except that upon the principles of the Islamic theologians there is a question regarding it. And it is to say: Why is it not permissible to say that at the first moment of raising one of the two surfaces from the other, the free agent creates a body between them? And upon this estimation, void does not occur at all.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is an objection (sual) directed against the preceding philosophical proof for void. Razi notes that the proof is unanswerable on the principles of the philosophers (who deny a free creator), but on the principles of Islamic theologians (who affirm a free agent, al-fa'il al-mukhtar), a valid question arises. The objection is: why cannot the free agent immediately create a body in the gap at the very instant the surfaces separate? If He does, then void never occurs—the gap is instantly filled. This objection undermines the necessity of void by appealing to divine power. The argument does not refute the logical possibility of void but challenges its necessity under Islamic theological commitments.

Key Terms
الفاعل المختار (al-fa'il al-mukhtar)
خلاء (khalaa)
سؤال (sual)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection proves that void is logically impossible.
Correction: The objection only shows that void is not necessary if God creates a body; it does not deny the logical possibility of void.

Checkpoint
What is the core of the Islamic theologians' objection to the void proof?
A) Void cannot exist because it is non-being.
B) The free agent can create a body in the gap, preventing void.
C) The surfaces cannot be perfectly planar.
D) The void would be infinitely divisible.

Key Takeaway
The Islamic theologians' objection shows that the proof for void fails if one accepts a free creator who can fill any potential gap at the moment of separation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as though God is constantly creating and sustaining every moment, or do you unconsciously rely on natural processes to 'fill the gaps' of your life? What would change if you truly believed He can create a body in an instant to prevent void?
?
When you encounter an impossibility or a gap in your understanding, do you allow for the possibility of divine intervention, or do you assume the physical explanation is exhaustive? How does this lesson challenge your default trust in secondary causes?
?
Reflect on a time when you sensed a 'void' in your life—an absence or emptiness. Did you turn to the Creator who can fill it instantly, or did you scramble for created things to fill the gap? What would it mean for you to entrust that void to the free agent today?

Proof for Vacuum and the Islamic Objection Based on Divine Power
Proof for vacuum from surfaces and Islamic counter-objection by divine creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical proof for the existence of vacuum from the consideration of surfaces and the distinctive Islamic objection that invokes divine omnipotence to fill any potential void.

Core Idea
Vacuum seems inevitable from surfaces, but divine power can create a body to fill the gap.

This lesson presents a fascinating debate between philosophers and Islamic theologians (mutakallimun) regarding the existence of vacuum. The philosophers propose a rigorous proof based on the geometry of surfaces, concluding that a vacuum must exist. The Islamic response, however, does not dispute the logical force of the proof on its own terms but introduces a theological principle: God, as the free agent, can directly create a body to prevent vacuum. This highlights a key difference in worldview—philosophers rely on necessary causal relations, while Islamists emphasize divine omnipotence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two cases considered in the proof.
2
Follow the two cases of the proof
The proof considers surfaces without pores and surfaces with pores. In both, a vacuum necessarily occurs. Identify the reasoning for each case.
3
Understand the Islamic objection
The author notes the proof is unanswerable on philosophical grounds, but Islamists can object: Why cannot God create a body at the moment of separation? This prevents vacuum.
This objection relies on the concept of a free agent (فاعل مختار).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة التاسعة والعشرون فرضنا الكلام في سطحين لا شيء من المسام فيهما وأيضا فبتقدير حصول المسام إلا أنه لا بد وأن يحصل بين كل منفذين من تلك الأجسام سطح متصل فالشيء الذي ينزل من المسام يكون حال كونه متصلا بطرف تلك الفرجة، لا يكون حاصلا في وسط السطح المتوسط فيما بين الفرجتين، فيكون ذلك الوسط خاليا لا محالة فثبت أن القول بالخلاء لازم على كل التقديرات. واعلم أن هذه الحجة لا يمكن الجواب عنها على أصول الفلاسفة، إلا أن على أصول الإسلاميين عليها سؤال. وهو أن يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن في أول وقت رفع أحد السطحين عن الآخر، يخلق الفاعل المختار فيما بينهما جسما؟ وعلى هذا التقدير لا يحصل الخلاء البتة.
The Twenty-Ninth Issue: We hypothesized speech about two surfaces with no pores in them, and also given the assumption of the existence of pores, it is inevitable that between every two openings of those bodies there is a contiguous surface. So the thing that descends from the pores, while it is touching the edge of that gap, is not present in the middle of the intermediate surface between the two gaps, so that middle is necessarily empty. Thus it is established that the statement of vacuum is necessary in all estimations. Know that this argument cannot be answered according to the principles of the philosophers, except that according to the principles of the Islamists there is an objection to it. It is said: 'Why is it not permissible to say that at the first moment of raising one of the two surfaces from the other, the free agent creates a body between them? On this estimation, no vacuum occurs at all.'
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the existence of vacuum from a hypothetical scenario involving two surfaces, then gives an Islamic objection. The proof considers two cases: surfaces without pores and surfaces with pores. In both cases, an empty middle space is necessary, so vacuum must exist. The author notes that this proof is unanswerable on philosophical principles, but on Islamic principles there is an objection: the free agent (God) could create a body in the gap at the moment of separation, preventing vacuum. This objection relies on divine omnipotence to fill any potential void.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Islamic objection disproves the philosophical proof, showing vacuum is impossible.
Correction: The author states the proof is unanswerable on philosophical principles; the objection only works on Islamic principles of divine omnipotence, not as a refutation of the proof's logical necessity within a purely philosophical framework.

Checkpoint
What is the Islamic objection to the proof for vacuum from surfaces?
A) Surfaces cannot be raised without pores.
B) The free agent can create a body to fill the gap, preventing vacuum.
C) Vacuum cannot be measured.
D) Motion in vacuum is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The philosophical proof for vacuum appears logically compelling, but Islamic theologians counter by appealing to divine omnipotence, which can fill any supposed void.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof for vacuum seems logically inevitable, but the Islamic objection reminds us that Allah can break natural patterns. Is there a situation in your life where you feel trapped by 'inevitable' circumstances? Have you truly considered that Allah can create a way out where no way exists? If not, what is stopping you from believing that today?
?
The philosophers assumed a closed system of cause and effect. Do you ever fall into the trap of thinking that your life runs on automatic patterns—like the necessity of failure after a mistake or the impossibility of change? How can you internalize that Allah is the free agent who can intervene at any moment, even when the evidence seems stacked against change?
?
When you hear the phrase 'free agent,' do you feel comfort or unease? Is it easier to rely on predictable causes (like medicine or effort) than on direct divine intervention? Examine your heart: where do you actually trust Allah's freedom to act, and where do you still rely on secondary causes as if they were necessary? Ask Allah to increase your tawakkul.

Motion in Vacuum Cannot Take Time
First part of second proof: motion in vacuum cannot take time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first half of Imam al-Razi's second argument against vacuum, showing that motion in a vacuum cannot occur in time.

Core Idea
If motion in vacuum took time, then resistance would be irrelevant, an impossibility.

Imam al-Razi presents a second argument against the existence of vacuum, focusing on the nature of motion. He argues that motion in a vacuum is impossible whether it takes time or not. In this lesson, we examine the first horn: why motion in a vacuum cannot occur in any finite time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the logical structure: assumption of vacuum leads to either time or no time.
Focus on the first part about motion in time.
2
Understand the proportional argument
The argument uses a proportion: if vacuum traversal takes 1 hour, and air traversal takes 10 hours, then a medium with proportionally less resistance would also take 1 hour, equating motion with and without resistance.
This is the key reductio ad absurdum.
3
See the absurdity
The conclusion is that motion with resistance would equal motion without resistance, which is impossible. Thus motion in vacuum cannot occur in time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية لهم : لو فرضنا الخلاء لكانت الحركة فيه إما أن تقع في زمان أو لا والقسمان باطلان فبطل القول بالخلاء. إنما قلنا : إن الحركة فيه يمتنع وقوعها في زمان؛ وذلك لأن المتحرك فيه كلما كان أرق كانت المعاوقة أقل، فكانت الحركة فيه لا محالة أسرع وإذا ثبت هذا، فلنفرض مائة ذراع من المسافة ولنفرض أنها لو كانت خلاء، لتم قطعها في ساعة واحدة، ولو كانت ملاء من الهواء، لتم قطعها في عشر ساعات . فإذا فرضنا ملاء أقل معاوقة من الهواء، بحيث تكون نسبة معاوقته إلى معاوقة الهواء، كنسبة زمان الحركة في الخلاء إلى الحركة في الهواء لزم أن يقع قطع تلك المسافة المملوءة من ذلك الملاء الرقيق في ساعة واحدة فتكون الحركة في الملاء مثل الحركة في الخلاء، فتكون الحركة مع المعاوقة كالحركة لا مع المعاوق، وذلك محال فثبت انه لو صح القول بالخلاء امتنع وقوع الحركة فيه في زمان. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع وقوع الحركة في الخلاء لا في زمان؛ لأن كل حركة فهي على مسافة وكل مسافة منقسمة. وإذا كان كذلك كانت الحركة إلى نصفها متقدمة على الحركة من نصفها إلى آخرها فثبت بما ذكرنا أن الحركة في الخلاء إما أن تحصل في زمان أو لا في زمان . وثبت فساد هذين القسمين، فثبت القطع بأن القول بوجود الخلاء محال باطل.
The second proof for them: If we assumed vacuum, then motion in it would either occur in time or not, and both divisions are invalid, so the statement of vacuum is invalid. We say: motion in it is impossible to occur in time; because the mover in it, the more rarified it is, the less resistance, so motion in it is necessarily faster. If this is established, let us assume a distance of one hundred cubits, and assume that if it were vacuum, it would be traversed in one hour, and if it were a plenum of air, it would be traversed in ten hours. So if we assume a plenum less resistant than air, such that the ratio of its resistance to that of air is like the ratio of the time of motion in vacuum to motion in air, it would be necessary that traversing that distance filled with that fine plenum occurs in one hour; thus motion in the plenum would be like motion in vacuum, so motion with resistance would be like motion without resistance, and that is impossible. Thus it is established that if the statement of vacuum were correct, motion in it would be impossible to occur in time. And we say: motion in vacuum is impossible to occur not in time; because every motion is over a distance, and every distance is divisible. If that is so, then motion to its half is prior to motion from its half to its end. Thus it is established by what we mentioned that motion in vacuum either occurs in time or not in time, and the corruption of both divisions is established, so it is decisively established that the statement of the existence of vacuum is impossible and invalid.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This second argument against vacuum uses motion. It argues that motion in a vacuum would have to take either time or no time, both impossible. First, if it takes time, then since vacuum offers no resistance, motion should be faster. By comparing a vacuum traversal (1 hour for 100 cubits) with a medium traversal (10 hours), one can postulate a medium with resistance proportionally less such that it also takes 1 hour. Then motion with resistance would equal motion without resistance, which is absurd. Therefore motion in vacuum cannot take time. Second, if it does not take time, motion would be instantaneous. But all motion spans a distance, and distance is divisible; so motion to the halfway point must precede motion to the endpoint, requiring time. Hence motion cannot be instantaneous. Thus vacuum is impossible.

Key Terms
خلاء
حركة
زمان
معاوقة
ملاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the second argument claim motion in vacuum cannot occur in time?
A) Because vacuum has no resistance, so motion would be infinitely fast.
B) Because it would entail motion with resistance equal to motion without resistance.
C) Because time is not divisible.
D) Because motion requires a medium.

Key Takeaway
Motion in a vacuum cannot occur in time because it would absurdly equate motion with and without resistance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument shows that an assumption (vacuum) leads to logical absurdity. What is one belief you hold that, if followed to its logical conclusion, would lead to a contradiction? Will you examine it honestly today and decide whether to reject it?
?
This proof uses proportional reasoning to reveal inconsistency. In your own life, are there inconsistencies between what you claim to believe and how you actually live? Identify one such inconsistency and commit to a concrete action this week to align your actions with your beliefs.
?
If motion in a vacuum cannot take time, then time itself is tied to resistance and medium. How does this reshape your understanding of the relationship between time and existence? Does your daily awareness of time reflect a deeper connection to the physical world, or is it just a schedule? Will you change how you perceive time after this lesson?

Motion in Vacuum Cannot Be Instantaneous
Second part of second proof: motion in vacuum cannot be instantaneous.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second horn of Imam al-Razi's second argument: motion in a vacuum cannot occur without time, due to the divisibility of distance.

Core Idea
Every distance is divisible, so motion must take time to cross parts.

Having shown that motion in a vacuum cannot take time, Imam al-Razi now addresses the possibility that it could be instantaneous. He argues that this too is impossible because any motion across a distance must have a before and after, implying temporal succession.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the argument against instantaneous motion.
2
Understand the divisibility argument
The argument states: every motion spans a distance; every distance is divisible; thus motion to the midpoint precedes motion from the midpoint, requiring time.
This refutes the idea of instantaneous motion.
3
Conclude both horns impossible
Since motion in vacuum can neither take time nor be instantaneous, vacuum itself is impossible.
This completes the second proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

We say: motion in it is impossible to occur in time; because the mover in it, the more rarified it is, the less resistance, so motion in it is necessarily faster. If this is established, let us assume a distance of one hundred cubits, and assume that if it were vacuum, it would be traversed in one hour, and if it were a plenum of air, it would be traversed in ten hours. So if we assume a plenum less resistant than air, such that the ratio of its resistance to that of air is like the ratio of the time of motion in vacuum to motion in air, it would be necessary that traversing that distance filled with that fine plenum occurs in one hour; thus motion in the plenum would be like motion in vacuum, so motion with resistance would be like motion without resistance, and that is impossible. Answer to the Second Argument: Motion and Time
Answer suggesting motion inherently requires time, resistance adds extra.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi defends the possibility of motion in a vacuum by distinguishing between the time required for motion itself and additional time due to resistance.

Core Idea
Motion always takes time; resistance only adds more.

In response to the second argument, which claimed that motion in a vacuum would be impossible because it would be instantaneous, Imam Razi offers a simple yet profound distinction. He suggests that motion, by its very nature, requires a certain amount of time, and any resistance from the medium merely adds extra time. This insight preserves the possibility of motion even in a vacuum, shifting the burden of proof back to the opponent.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it is structured as a rhetorical question. Let the author's own phrasing sink in before analyzing.
The passage is short but dense; pay attention to the two clauses separated by 'and because of...'
2
Distinguish the two components of time
Identify the two amounts of time mentioned: one that is intrinsic to motion as such, and another that is added due to resistance in the medium. Understand that even without resistance (i.e., in a vacuum), motion still requires the first amount.
This is the key logical move: it rejects the assumption that motion in vacuum would be instantaneous.
3
Apply the answer to the original argument
Consider how this answer undermines the second argument. The argument tried to prove that motion in a vacuum is impossible by showing it would be instantaneous. Razi's response shows that even in a vacuum, motion takes time, so the impossibility is not proven.
The point is not to prove that vacuum motion is possible, but to show that the argument against it fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن الثاني: لم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن الحركة من حيث إنها حركة تستدعي قدرا من الزمان، وبسبب ما في المسافة من المعاوقة، تستدعي قدرًا آخر من الزمان؟
And the answer to the second: Why is it not permissible to say that motion, insofar as it is motion, requires an amount of time, and because of what is in the distance of resistance, it requires another amount of time?
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This is the answer to the second argument. It proposes that motion inherently demands a certain amount of time simply because it is motion (i.e., traversal of distance), and additional resistance adds extra time. Thus, when the first argument compared motion in vacuum to motion in a medium, it wrongly assumed that the base time is zero. The answer suggests that even in a vacuum, motion would take a base time, so the impossibility of motion in vacuum is not proven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Motion in a vacuum would be instantaneous because there is no resistance.
Correction: Motion inherently requires time; resistance only adds extra time. Even in a vacuum, motion takes a base amount of time.

C) It is impossible.
D) It is faster than in a medium.

Key Takeaway
Motion inherently requires time; resistance only adds additional time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Consider a time you became frustrated because your efforts were met with resistance. How does the distinction between base time and extra time shift your perspective on that struggle? What commitment can you make to view delays not as failures but as part of the necessary time for motion?

Razi's Proof Against Void: Motion Requires Time
Razi proves motion in void requires time, refuting void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that motion in a void cannot occur without time, establishing the impossibility of void.

Core Idea
Motion always takes time because distance is divisible; void makes this impossible.

Imam Razi presents a sophisticated argument against the existence of void (khalā'). He shows that even if void existed, motion in it would be impossible because motion requires time, but in void there is no resistance to measure time. This introduces a key kalam proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice Razi's two-part argument: first from absurd equivalence, then from divisibility of distance.
2
Identify the two arguments
Razi first gives a reductio: if a fine medium exists, motion in it is like void, so resistance = no resistance. Then he gives direct proof: distance is divisible, so motion takes time.
3
Understand the conclusion
Both ways lead to impossibility, so void cannot exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك الملاء الرقيق في ساعة واحدة فتكون الحركة في الملاء مثل الحركة في الخلاء، فتكون الحركة مع المعارق كهي لا مع المعاوق، وذلك محال فثبت انه لو صح القول بالخلاء امتنع وقوع الحركة فيه في زمان.
وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع وقوع الحركة في الخلاء لا في زمان؛ لأن كل حركة فهي على مسافة وكل مسافة منقسمة. وإذا كان كذلك كانت الحركة إلى نصفها متقدمة على [؟] ومتى كان كذلك كانت الحركة واقعة في الزمان. ثم [؟] الحركة من نصفها إلى آخرها فثبت بما ذكرنا أن الحركة في الخلاء إما أن تحصل في زمان أو لا في زمان . وثبت فساد هذين القسمين، فثبت القطع بأن القول بوجود الخلاء محال باطل.
That rarefied medium in one hour, so the motion in the medium would be like the motion in the void, so the motion with resistance would be like it without resistance, and that is impossible. So it is established that if the statement of void were valid, the occurrence of motion in it would be impossible in time. And we only said: it is impossible for motion to occur in the void not in time, because every motion is over a distance and every distance is divisible. If that is so, then the motion to its half is prior to [?] and whenever that is so, the motion occurs in time. Then [?] the motion from its half to its other half, so it is established by what we mentioned that motion in the void either occurs in time or not in time. Both divisions have been proven false, so it is established decisively that the statement of the existence of void is impossible and false.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a proof by Imam Razi against the existence of void (kala'). He begins by referencing a previous scenario: if there were a very fine medium (mala' raqiq) that offers minimal resistance, motion through it would be like motion through absolute void—i.e., with resistance equivalent to no resistance. This is impossible, so assuming void leads to absurdity. He then gives a direct proof: motion always occurs over a distance, and every distance is divisible. Therefore, when a body moves across a distance, it must first traverse half of it, and that half-motion occurs before the entire motion. This priority implies that motion takes time. Hence, motion in void must occur either in time or without time. Since the latter is impossible (motion requires time due to distance divisibility) and the former would require resistance of some kind (which void lacks), both options fail. Thus the concept of void is impossible.

Key Terms
خلاء
حركة
زمان
مسافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Razi denies motion can be instantaneous in any context.
Correction: Razi argues that even in void, motion requires time because distance is divisible; he does not claim motion is never instantaneous, but that in this scenario it cannot be.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Razi gives for why motion in void cannot occur without time?
A) Because void has no resistance
B) Because every distance is divisible and motion to half precedes the rest
C) Because the free agent can only act in time
D) Because void is uniform

Key Takeaway
Razi's argument shows that motion always requires time because distance is divisible, making the existence of void impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi proves that all motion requires time because distance is divisible. In your spiritual journey, do you treat growth as if it should be instantaneous—like motion in a void—or do you accept that every step toward Allah requires patient traversal of distance? What half-distances have you neglected because you wanted the whole without the time?
?
If the concept of void leads to absurdity, what 'voids' in your own life—areas where you believe there is no resistance, no accountability, no consequence—have led you to act as though your actions need no time to bear fruit? How will you fill those voids with the reality of divine order?
?
Razi's proof forces you to acknowledge that even if all obstacles were removed, motion still demands time. When you ask Allah for a change, do you assume that removing worldly barriers is enough, or do you recognize that the journey itself is divinely ordained with stages? Which stage are you rushing through without honoring its required time?
